Proof of the Impossibility of Two Creators
Al-Nasafi proves the impossibility of two creators through exhaustive case analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that the world cannot have more than one creator, as demonstrated by al-Nasafi's exhaustive case analysis.

Core Idea
Multiple creators logically impossible because every possibility leads to contradiction.

Al-Nasafi builds on earlier proofs to tackle a fundamental question: can the world have more than one maker? Using pure logic, he shows that any scenario with two creators results in impossibility or incapacity, thereby affirming the oneness of God. This lesson walks through his rigorous argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Context and premise
Recall the previous proof that the world must have a maker. Now we ask whether it can have more than one. Read the opening lines of the passage to set the stage.
Notice the phrase 'إما أن كان صانع العالم واحداً أو أكثر من واحد' — this is the question.
2
Initial three possibilities
The passage divides the scenario of two creators into three logical cases: both unable, one unable, or both able. Identify and understand each case.
These are listed as 'إما أن يكون كل واحد منهما قادراً... إما أن لم يكن... إما أن كان أحدهما...'
3
Subcases when both are able
When both are able, there are subcases: cooperation vs. independence, and then what happens when one creates. Follow the argument carefully.
This is the most detailed part; take your time.
4
Conclusion and significance
After exhausting all possibilities, al-Nasafi concludes that two creators are impossible. Reflect on why this proof is central to tawhid.
The final line: 'فبطل إذا أن يكون للعالم صانعان'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ثبت بما مر من الدلائل أن العالم لابد له من صانع، لاستحالة اختصاص ما يجوز عليه العدم بالوجود، وتبدل الحال من العدم إلى الوجود بعد أن كان معدوماً بلا مخصص خصصه به على ما مر بيانه فبعد ذلك نقول: إما أن كان صانع العالم واحداً أو أكثر من واحد، ولا جائز أن يكون أكثر من واحد، لأنه لو كان للعالم صانعان وهما على ما هو معلوم لو وجد لكان في حالة الوجود عرضاً أو جوهراً، لكان الأمر لا يخلو إما أن يكون كل واحد منهما قادراً على إيجاده، وإما أن لم يكن كل واحد منهما قادراً على إيجاده، وإما أن كان أحدهما قادراً على إيجاده دون الآخر. فإن لم يكن كل واحد منهما قادراً على إيجاده مع أنه مقدور في نفسه فإذا كل واحد منهما كان عاجزاً لزوال قدرته عما هو المقدور في نفسه، ولن يكون ذلك إلا عن عجز كما أن زوال العلم عما يصح تعلقه به لن يكون إلا عن جهل والعاجز لا يكون إلهاً، فإذا بطلت ألوهيتهما. ولو كان أحدهما قادراً على إيجاده ولم يكن الآخر قادراً، فهذا الثاني لا يكون إلهاً، ولو كان جميعاً قادرين، إما أن قدر كل واحد منهما على إيجاده على الانفراد والاستبداد، وإما أن قدرا على ذلك على طريق التعاون. فإن قدرا على طريق التعاون دون الانفراد كان كل واحد منهما عاجزاً لزوال قدرته عما هو مقدور في نفسه، ولو قدر كل واحد منهما على الانفراد ثم أوجده أحدهما إما أن زالت عن إيجاده قدرة الآخر وإما أن لم تزل، فإن لم تزل قدرة الآخر فهذا محال، لأن إيجاد الموجود محال، والمحال لا يدخل تحت القدرة، وإن زالت قدرة الآخر عن إيجاده بعدما كان ذلك مقدوراً بسبب إيجاد صاحبه فقد عجز صاحبه إذ أزال قدرته عما هو مقدور له، ومن نفذ سلطان غيره عليه بالتعجيز فهو مقدور له داخل تحت تصرفه وهذا مما يستحيل على الله تعالى، فبطل إذا أن يكون للعالم صانعان.
And if it has been established by the proofs that have passed that the world inevitably has a maker, due to the impossibility of that which admits non-existence being specified with existence, and the change of state from non-existence to existence after it was non-existent without a specifier that specified it with it as has been explained, then after that we say: either the maker of the world is one or more than one, and it is not possible that it be more than one. Because if the world had two makers, and they are as is known (if it existed it would be in the state of existence an accident or a substance), then the matter would not be free from either each one of them being able to bring it into existence, or each one of them not being able to bring it into existence, or one of them being able to bring it into existence without the other. If each one of them were not able to bring it into existence while it is possible in itself, then each one of them would be incapable due to the removal of his power over what is possible in itself, and that would only be from incapacity, just as the removal of knowledge from that to which it can be attached would only be from ignorance, and the incapable cannot be a god, so their divinity is invalidated. And if one of them were able to bring it into existence and the other were not able, then this second would not be a god. And if both were able, either each one of them was able to bring it into existence independently and alone, or they were able to do that by way of cooperation. If they were able by way of cooperation without independence, then each one of them would be incapable due to the removal of his power over what is possible in itself. And if each one of them was able independently, then one of them brought it into existence, either the power of the other over bringing it into existence ceases or it does not cease. If the power of the other does not cease, this is impossible, because bringing into existence what already exists is impossible, and the impossible does not fall under power. And if the power of the other over bringing it into existence ceases after it was possible due to the bringing into existence by his fellow, then his fellow has become incapable, since he removed his power over what was possible for him, and the one whose power over him by disabling is overcome is himself under his control and subject to his disposal, and this is impossible for Allah. So it is invalidated that the world should have two makers.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the oneness of God (tawhid) by demonstrating the impossibility of two creators for the world. The author, al-Nasafi, structures his argument by first restating the conclusion from previous proofs: the world must have a maker. Then he poses the question: is the maker one or more than one? He argues that more than one is impossible. He then exhausts the logical possibilities for two creators. 1) If both are unable to create the world, then each is incapable and cannot be divine. 2) If only one is able, the other is not divine. 3) If both are able, there are two subcases: a) they cooperate (neither can act alone) – then each is incapable because each depends on the other. b) each is independently able to create the world. If both are independent, then if one creates, either the other's power over that act remains or ceases. If it remains, then the other would be trying to create something already existing, which is impossible. If it ceases, then the other's power has been disabled by the first, meaning the first has power over the second, which is impossible for God. Thus every possibility leads to contradiction, proving that the world can have only one creator.

Key Terms
صانع
قدرة
عجز
إله
توحيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Two gods could cooperate harmoniously to create the world.
Correction: Al-Nasafi shows that if they cooperate and cannot act independently, each is dependent and incapable, which contradicts divinity. If they are independent, one will disable the other. Thus, cooperation is impossible for divine beings.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi's argument, if two creators are both independently able and one creates the world, what happens to the power of the other?
A) It remains intact because both are equally powerful.
B) It ceases because creating what already exists is impossible.
C) It becomes greater because the creation is already done.
D) It becomes irrelevant because the world already exists.

Key Takeaway
Logical proof demonstrates that any scenario with two creators leads to contradiction or incapacity, affirming the necessity of one creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even unconsciously, attributed some power or control in your life to someone or something other than Allah? How does this logical proof challenge that subtle shirk? Are you willing to repent from it right now?
?
The proof shows that any incapacity disqualifies a being from divinity. In your daily life, where do you act as if you are independent of Allah, as if you alone sustain yourself? What is one concrete step you can take today to make your reliance on Allah more real?
?
If you truly internalized that there can be no partner with Allah in any act of creation or control, would you still fear the opinions of people or cling to your own plans as if they could override Allah's decree? What would change in your heart if you lived by this proof?

Proof Against Two Creators via Cooperation
Nasafi proves impossibility of two creators by cooperation and individual action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's rational argument against the possibility of two creators for the world, based on the scenarios of cooperation and individual action.

Core Idea
Two creators cannot exist because both would be either dependent or controlling.

Nasafi presents a proof that eliminates cooperation and individual action as possibilities for dual creators. By analyzing both scenarios, he demonstrates logical contradictions that render the notion of two creators impossible. This lesson walks through that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Notice the logical structure of the proof.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the cooperation scenario
Focus on the first scenario: if two creators cooperate, each is individually incapable of the whole act. Why is this a problem?
Incapacity (عجز) is impossible for a perfect creator.
3
Analyze the individual action scenario
Now examine the second scenario: each acts alone. When one creates, what happens to the other's ability? Consider both sub-cases.
Sub-case 1: ability remains → impossible to create what already exists. Sub-case 2: ability removed → the first incapacitates the second.
4
See the conclusion
Both scenarios lead to logical impossibilities, so the existence of two creators is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك على طريق التعاون (۱) (فإن قدرا على طريق التعاون ) (۲) دون الانفراد كان كل واحد منهما عاجزا لزوال قدرته عما هو مقدور في نفسه، ولو قدر كل واحد منهما على الانفراد ثم أوجده أحدهما إما أن زالت عن إيجاده قدرة الآخر وإما أن لم تزل، فإن لم تزل قدرة الأخرى فهذا محال ، لأن إيجاد الموجود محال، والمحال لا يدخل تحت القدرة، وإن زالت قدرة الآخر عن إيجاده بعدما كان ذلك مقدورا بسبب إيجاد صاحبه فقد عجز صاحبه إذ أزال قدرته عما هو مقدور له، ومن نفذ سلطان غيره عليه بالتعجيز فهو مقدور له داخل تحت تصرفه وهذا مما يستحيل على الله تعالى، فبطل إذا أن يكون للعالم صانعان
That [is] by way of cooperation (1) (if they were able by way of cooperation) (2) without individual action, each one of them would be incapable due to the removal of his ability from what is possible in itself. And if each one of them were capable individually, and then one of them brings it into existence, either the ability of the other is removed from its bringing into existence, or it is not removed. If the ability of the other is not removed, then this is impossible, because bringing into existence what already exists is impossible, and the impossible does not fall under ability. And if the ability of the other is removed from its bringing into existence after it had been possible due to the bringing into existence by its companion, then its companion has become incapable since he removed his ability from what was possible for him. And one whose authority over another is executed by incapacitating him, then he is controlled and under his disposal, and this is impossible for Allah, the Exalted. Thus it is false that the world has two creators.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is a proof against the existence of two creators for the world. The argument proceeds by considering two scenarios: either the two creators cooperate in creating the world or they act individually. If they cooperate (طريق التعاون), each alone is incapable of the whole act, meaning each is dependent—impossible for a perfect creator. If they act individually, then when one creates a thing, the other's ability to create that same thing either remains or is removed. If it remains, creating it again would be impossible (إيجاد الموجود محال), and the impossible does not fall under power. If it is removed, then the first creator has incapacitated the second, implying power over the other's ability—also impossible for God. Thus, the existence of two creators is false (فبطل أن يكون للعالم صانعان).

Key Terms
صانعان
قدرة
إيجاد
تعجيز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think cooperation between two creators might imply mutual completion, making them both capable together.
Correction: The proof shows cooperation forces each to be individually incapable of the whole act, which is a deficiency incompatible with divine perfection.

Checkpoint
What does the proof establish if two creators cooperate in creating the world?
A) They are both fully capable.
B) Each is incapable of the whole act, so each is deficient.
C) They must create different objects.
D) Cooperation is the only possibility.

Key Takeaway
The logical impossibility of two creators is demonstrated by analyzing cooperation and individual action, both leading to contradictions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation beyond your control, do you turn to Allah alone, or do you seek help from created beings as if they could create outcomes? Reflect on a recent moment of fear or need: did your action match your belief that only Allah has ultimate power? How will you train your heart to rely solely on Him starting today?
?
The proof shows that any other supposed creator must be either dependent or powerless. Have you ever, even subconsciously, attributed independent power to anyone or anything—a person, a system, or your own abilities? How does this logical demonstration reshape your conviction in Allah's exclusive sovereignty? What step will you take this week to uproot any hidden shirk in your heart?
?
This proof is not just intellectual; it demands that your heart submits to Allah's sole authority. Is there any area of your life where you act as if you are the creator of your own success or failure, controlling outcomes by your own power? How can you practically affirm 'There is no creator but Allah' in your daily decisions, especially in moments of pride or despair? What specific dua or action will you use to remind yourself?

The Motion and Rest Argument Against Two Creators
Nasafi presents a second proof and refutes an objection about capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's second proof against two creators using motion and rest, including his refutation of the objection that creating something ends the creator's power.

Core Idea
Executing divine power is not its removal; two creators would lead to logical impossibility.

This lesson presents a second rational proof against the existence of two creators. Building on the previous argument, Nasafi uses the concepts of motion and rest to show that two creators would inevitably contradict each other. He also addresses an objection that might arise about the nature of divine power after creation.

Guided Path
1
Explore the objection and refutation
Read the first part where Nasafi rejects the idea that creating something ends the creator's power. Understand why executing power is not incapacitation.
The objection is that after creating, the creator's ability ceases. Nasafi argues that is false.
2
Understand the motion-rest dilemma
Grasp the scenario: we consider a body and ask if each of two creators can create motion or rest in it at a future time.
This sets up a logical test for the claim of two creators.
3
Analyze the forced choices
Follow the two possible answers and their consequences. If both can, then one creates motion and the other creates rest simultaneously—impossible. If the second cannot, he is incapacitated.
Both outcomes contradict the assumption of two omnipotent creators.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقال إن الواحد لما أوجده فقد زالت قدرته أيضا عن الإيجاد لاستحالة إيجاد الموجود ، لما أن إيجاد ما هو قادر على إيجاده بتنفيذ القدرة، وكيف يكون تنفيذ القدرة تعجيزا وإزالة لها ؟ فأما الصانعان فكل واحد منهما قادر وله قدرة على حدة، فكان القول بنفاذ إحداهما إزالة للأخرى ضرورة فكان تعجيزا ونقرر هذه الدلالة أيضا من وجه آخر فيقال: إنا نعين جسما من الأجسام فنقول: هل يقدر كل واحد منهما على أن يخلق فيه في وقت ما فيما يستقبل من الأوقات حركة أو سكونا ؟ فإن قالوا: لا. فقد عجزوهما، وإن قالوا: نعم. قلنا: لو خلق أحدهما في ذلك الوقت بعينه فيه حركة هل يقدر الآخر على (2) أن يخلق فيه في عين ذلك الوقت سكونا ؟ فإن (1) قالوا: نعم. فقد ارتكبوا محالا، حيث جوزوا اجتماع الحركة والسكون في وقت واحد في محل واحد وإن قالوا: لا. فقد جعلوه عاجزا عما كان عليه قادرا، وقدرته زائلة عما كانت عليه ،ثابتة، وهذا هو التعجيز وهو محال على الصانع
And it is not said that when one created it, his ability to bring into existence also ceased due to the impossibility of bringing into existence what exists, because bringing into existence what he is able to bring into existence is by executing the ability, and how can executing the ability be an incapacitation and removal of it? As for the two creators, each of them is capable and has a separate ability, so saying that one of them is effective necessarily removes the other, so it is an incapacitation. And we also establish this proof from another angle: we say: we specify a body from among bodies and say: Is each of them able to create in it at a particular time in the future a motion or rest? If they say: No, then they have made them both incapable. If they say: Yes, we say: If one of them created in it at that exact time a motion, is the other able to create in it at that same time a rest? If they say: Yes, then they have committed an impossibility, since they allow the conjunction of motion and rest at one time in one place. If they say: No, then they have made him incapable of what he was able to do, and his ability is removed from what it was upon, [while it is] established, and this is incapacitation, and it is impossible for the Creator.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage contains a second proof against two creators, preceded by a refutation of an objection. The objection claims that when one creator brings something into existence, his own ability to create it again ceases (because re-creation is impossible). The answer is that executing one's ability is not an incapacitation; it is the fulfillment of power. Then the proof is restated: take any body, and ask whether each creator can create motion or rest in it at a future time. If they cannot, they are incapable. If they can, then suppose one creates motion at a specific time. Can the other create rest at that same time in the same body? If yes, they would combine two opposites (حركة وسكون) simultaneously—impossible. If no, then the second is incapacitated after being able. Thus the impossibility of two creators is reiterated.

Key Terms
حركة
سكون
تعجيز
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: After creating something, a creator's power is exhausted or removed.
Correction: Executing power is not its removal; it is the actualization of ability. The objection is false.

Checkpoint
What does the second proof conclude if one creator creates motion in a body and the other attempts to create rest at the same time?
A) Both acts can occur simultaneously.
B) The second creator is incapacitated or an impossibility follows.
C) The body can be both moving and still.
D) The first creator's power is removed.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of two creators is proven by the logical impossibility of them acting consistently on a single body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'La ilaha illallah', do you truly believe that no other being could ever have power to move even a single atom without Allah's permission? This passage proves the logical absurdity of two creators. Has this proof solidified your certainty such that no doubt remains in your heart about the exclusivity of Allah's power? If not, what lingering thoughts or influences from the world still weaken your conviction?
?
The argument refutes the idea that creating something diminishes the creator's power. Reflect on your own life: do you ever act as if obeying Allah or worshipping Him somehow 'uses up' your energy or freedom? How does Nasafi's point—that executing power is not its removal—challenge the way you approach your worship and duties?
?
Imagine yourself standing before Allah on the Day of Judgment, and He asks you: 'Did you truly believe that none besides Me can create any motion or rest?' Would your daily actions—the things you fear, rely on, or hope from others—betray a hidden belief in other creators? What one step can you take today to erase any trace of that from your heart?

Distinction Between One and Two Creators Regarding Power
Nasafi refutes an objection about power ceasing after creation and distinguishes between one and two creators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between a single creator and two creators regarding the execution of power, and why the objection about power ceasing does not apply to the case of two creators.

Core Idea
For one creator, executing power is acting; for two, it is disabling.

This passage addresses a subtle objection: if a creator's power ceases after creating, would that not imply deficiency? Nasafi responds by distinguishing between one and two creators. He shows that for a single creator, power ceasing after creation is not disabling because it is simply the completion of action. But for two creators, if one's power is executed, it necessarily removes the other's ability, which is true disabling.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the objection and response
In the passage, the opponent claims that when one creator creates, his power ceases. Find how Nasafi responds, and note the key distinction he makes.
Look for the phrase 'فأما الصانعان' which introduces the two-creator case.
3
Analyze the distinction
Nasafi differentiates between one creator and two creators. For one, executing power is not disabling; for two, one's execution disables the other. Understand why this distinction matters.
Think about what 'disabling' (تعجيز) means in each context.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider why this argument refutes the idea that God's power is limited after creation. How does it uphold the perfection of God's power?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقال إن الواحد لما أوجده فقد زالت قدرته أيضا عن الإيجاد لاستحالة إيجاد الموجود ، لما أن إيجاد ما هو قادر على إيجاده بتنفيذ القدرة، وكيف يكون تنفيذ القدرة تعجيزا وإزالة لها ؟ فأما الصانعان فكل واحد منهما قادر وله قدرة على حدة، فكان القول بنفاذ إحداهما إزالة للأخرى ضرورة فكان تعجيزا
And it cannot be said that when the one creates, his power also ceases from creating because of the impossibility of creating what already exists, because his creating what he is able to create is by executing the power. And how can executing the power be disabling and removal of it? As for the two creators, each one of them is powerful and has a separate power, so the statement that one of them is executed (i.e., his power is effective) is a removal of the other necessarily, so it is disabling.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is an objection and answer. The opponent claims that when a single creator creates something, his power to create that specific thing ceases, but this is not considered disabling. The author responds by distinguishing between one and two creators. For a single creator, executing power is simply acting; it does not remove power, because power remains to create other things. However, for two creators, if one executes his power, it necessarily removes the other's power because the other cannot act in the same locus; thus, it is disabling. This distinction shows that the objection does not apply to the case of two creators.

Key Terms
قدرة
تعجيز
إيجاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a creator's power ceases after creating, that shows weakness.
Correction: For a single creator, power ceasing after creating is not a sign of weakness because it is simply the end of that specific act; the power remains to create other things.

Checkpoint
What is the key difference between a single creator and two creators regarding the execution of power?
A) For one, executing power removes power entirely; for two, it does not.
B) For one, executing power is not disabling; for two, one's execution disables the other.
C) For one, power ceases after creation; for two, power remains.
D) There is no difference.

Key Takeaway
The execution of power by a single creator is not disabling, whereas for two creators, one's execution disables the other.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does the distinction between one and two creators challenge any hidden assumption you might have that Allah's power is like human power—something that can be exhausted or shared? What would it mean for your tawheed if you unconsciously thought someone else could act independently alongside Allah?
?
When you face a situation where you feel your own 'power' is limited or has failed, do you ever resent Allah as if He did not use His power for you? How can this lesson's teaching—that Allah's power is never disabling—reshape your response to hardship?
?
If you truly believed that no one else has any power to create or sustain anything except Allah, would your fear of people's opinions or your reliance on them vanish? What is one specific habit you will change this week to reflect that belief?

intermediate
6 min
Proof from the Impossibility of Simultaneous Motion and Rest
Nasafi proves the impossibility of two gods by examining motion and rest.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that two omnipotent gods cannot exist because they would have to create contradictory states like motion and rest in the same body at the same time.

Core Idea
Two gods cannot both be omnipotent because they could contradict each other.

This lesson presents a clever logical demonstration from Imam Nasafi showing the impossibility of two gods. By considering a simple body and the ability to create motion or rest in it, a chain of questions leads to an unavoidable contradiction. The argument elegantly proves that only one omnipotent Creator can exist.

Guided Path
1
Understand the setup
Read the passage carefully. Notice that the argument begins by picking any body and asking whether each of the two supposed gods can create motion or rest in it at a future time.
This sets up the premise of omnipotence.
2
Trace the first dilemma
If they cannot create either, they are not omnipotent. If they can, we proceed to the next question. Pay attention to how the author forces a choice.
3
Analyze the second dilemma
If one god creates motion at a specific time, can the other create rest at the exact same time? The answer leads to either contradiction or disability. See how each option is impossible for a god.
This is the core of the proof.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Since both options lead to impossibility, the original assumption of two gods must be false. The proof is complete and concise.
This is an example of reasoning by contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونقرر هذه الدلالة أيضا من وجه آخر فيقال: إنا نعين جسما من الأجسام فنقول: هل يقدر كل واحد منهما على أن يخلق فيه في وقت ما فيما يستقبل من الأوقات حركة أو سكونا ؟ فإن قالوا: لا. فقد عجزوهما، وإن قالوا: نعم. قلنا: لو خلق أحدهما في ذلك الوقت بعينه فيه حركة هل يقدر الآخر على أن يخلق فيه في عين ذلك الوقت سكونا ؟ فإن قالوا: نعم. فقد ارتكبوا محالا، حيث جوزوا اجتماع الحركة والسكون في وقت واحد في محل واحد وإن قالوا: لا. فقد جعلوه عاجزا عما كان عليه قادرا، وقدرته زائلة عما كانت عليه ثابتة، وهذا هو التعجيز وهو محال على الصانع
And we also establish this proof from another aspect: it is said: we specify a body among bodies and we say: Is each of the two able to create in it at a certain future time motion or rest? If they say: No, then they have declared both incapable. If they say: Yes, we say: If one of them creates in that exact time motion in it, is the other able to create in the same exact time rest in it? If they say: Yes, then they have committed an impossibility, since they permit the conjunction of motion and rest at one time in one locus. If they say: No, then they have made him incapable of what he was able to do, and his power has ceased from what it was upon, and this is disabling, and disabling of the Creator is impossible.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage presents a second angle for the proof of oneness. The author sets up a logical dilemma. Consider any specific body. Ask whether each of the supposed two gods can create either motion or rest in it at a future time. If they cannot, they are not omnipotent. If they can, then test whether one can create motion while the other creates rest at the same time. If they answer yes, that would require the impossible conjunction of opposites. If no, then the second god becomes incapable of what he was able to do, which implies disability, impossible for a god. Thus, the existence of two gods is impossible.

Key Terms
حركة
سكون
محل
ضد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that two gods could coordinate their actions to avoid contradiction.
Correction: The argument shows that even the logical possibility of contradictory acts (e.g., one creating motion and the other creating rest simultaneously) is sufficient to prove impossibility, because omnipotence includes the ability to do so, and any restriction would negate omnipotence.

Checkpoint
What contradictory states would be required if two gods simultaneously willed motion and rest in the same body?
A) Motion and rest in the same body at different times.
B) Motion and rest in the same body at the same time.
C) Neither motion nor rest.
D) Only motion.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of two omnipotent gods is proven by the logical contradiction of simultaneous motion and rest in one body.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof shows that Allah cannot be incapacitated. When you face a situation you think is hopeless, do you truly believe He is still fully able to act? What would change in your dua tonight if you internalized this certainty?
?
If two gods are impossible because of contradiction, what about the 'gods' in your life—like career, reputation, or relationships—that sometimes demand your ultimate trust? How will you demote them today to affirm Allah's exclusive power?
?
This argument rests on the impossibility of opposites coexisting. In your heart, do you try to hold contradictory loyalties—loving Allah yet clinging to sin? Which 'rest' will you remove so that only His 'motion' occupies your soul?

Proof from Composition for Divine Oneness
Nasafi argues that two gods would each be composed, proving oneness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Nasafi's argument that multiple gods would be composed and thus contingent, establishing that Allah is one.

Core Idea
If there were two gods, each would be a composite—a sign of contingency.

This passage presents a classical argument for tawheed using the concept of composition. Nasafi argues that the very idea of multiple necessary beings requires each to have a common necessary aspect and a unique distinguishing aspect, which together make them composite—a clear sign of being created. The reasoning is compact but powerful.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the logical flow: hypothesis, implication, conclusion.
2
Identify the two components of each god
Find where Nasafi says each god would have a shared part (wajib al-wujud) and a unique part (tashakhkhus). These two together lead to composition.
Composition here is not physical but conceptual: a combination of aspects.
3
Understand why composition implies huduth
Nasafi asserts that composition is a sign of origination. Reflect on why only contingent things can be composed of parts.
The necessary being must be simple, without internal distinctions.
4
Draw the conclusion
If multiple gods lead to composition, and composition leads to contingency, then multiple gods are impossible. The necessary being must be one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانيا: لو وجد إلهان كان كل واحد منهما مركبا والتركيب من أمارات الحدوث فبطل ما أدى إليه وثبت أنه تعالى واحد وذلك لأن تعدد الإله يستدعى أمرين اشتراكهما في وجوب الوجود وتميز كل إله بتشخص يخالف تشخص الآخر وحينئذ يلزم تركب كل إله ومما به الاشتراك ومما به الامتياز فلو تعدد الإله للزم التركب.
Second: If there were two gods, each of them would be composed, and composition is among the signs of origination. So what leads to that is invalid, and it is established that He, exalted, is one. That is because multiplicity of gods requires two matters: their sharing in the necessity of existence, and each god's distinction by an individuation that differs from the other's individuation. Then, composition of each god from that by which they share and that by which they are distinguished necessarily follows. Thus, if there were multiplicity of gods, composition would be necessary.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This is the second proof, an argument from composition. If there were multiple gods, they would all share the attribute of necessary existence (common essence), but each must also have a unique individuation (tashakhkhs) to distinguish it from others. This combination of a common part and a distinguishing part results in composition (tarkib). Composition is a sign of being originated (hadath), because only originated things are composed of parts. Therefore, the existence of two gods is impossible, and God must be one.

Key Terms
تركيب
تشخص
وجوب الوجود
حدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Composition only applies to physical objects, so a non-physical being like God could not be composite.
Correction: Nasafi uses composition in a metaphysical sense: any being that has distinguishable aspects (like a shared essence and a unique individuation) is composite, regardless of physicality.

Checkpoint
What does composition (tarkib) indicate according to the author?
A) Necessity of existence
B) Individuation
C) Origination (hadath)
D) Omnipotence

Key Takeaway
The necessary being cannot be composite, so any multiplicity would force composition and thus contingency; therefore, God must be one.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is absolutely simple and cannot be divided or composed, what does that mean for the divided loyalties in your own heart? Where have you tried to serve both God and something else, as if there were two ultimate authorities? Today, choose one area where you will simplify your devotion.
?
The proof shows that any 'composition' in God would imply dependence. Your own soul is composed of body and spirit, desires and duties—you are contingent. Do you live in humble dependence on the One who is not composite? What does that dependence look like in your next decision?
?
Nasafi argues that multiplicity in the divine is absurd. Yet how often do you treat your own time and energy as if they belong to multiple masters? Name one 'second god'—a pursuit, a person, or a comfort—that you functionally elevate alongside Allah. What step will you take today to demote it?

Third Proof: The Impossibility of Two Gods Based on Sufficiency
Nasafi presents a trilemma: either one god suffices or both are needed, leading to deficiency in either case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the existence of two gods leads to a logical contradiction through the trilemma of sufficiency or mutual need.

Core Idea
Two gods would either be redundant or mutually dependent — both contradict divinity.

This third proof from Nasafi is a crisp logical argument that eliminates the possibility of multiple gods. The argument is a disjunction: if two gods exist, either one is sufficient to create the world or both are needed. Each case leads to an absurdity. Let's examine the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument and its translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage carefully. Then read the English translation to grasp the logical flow. Note the two branches of the disjunction.
The argument is short but dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two possibilities
The passage presents two mutually exclusive possibilities: either one god alone suffices for creation, or both are needed together. Recognize how each leads to a contradiction.
3
Reflect on why each possibility is impossible
For the first possibility, if one suffices, the other is superfluous—contradicting divine necessity. For the second, if both are needed, each is incapable alone—contradicting divine power. Conclude that two gods cannot exist.
This argument is a classic in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثا: لو وجد إلهان فلا يخلو إما أن يكون أحدهما كافيا في إيجاد العالم وحينئذ يكن الآخر صانعا، وإما أن لا يكون بل لابد منهما فيكون كل واحد منهما عاجزا والعاجز لا يكون إلها.
Third: If there were two gods, then either one of them is sufficient for bringing the world into existence, in which case the other would be a creator (unnecessarily), or he is not sufficient, but both are needed, in which case each of them would be incapable, and the incapable cannot be a god.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This is the third proof, a simple disjunctive argument. If two gods exist, the creation of the world either requires both or not. If one alone is sufficient, then the other is redundant and unnecessary, which contradicts the perfection of divinity. If both are necessary, then each is dependent on the other, meaning each is deficient and incapable of acting alone, which is impossible for a god. Thus, two gods cannot exist.

Key Terms
كاف
عاجز
إيجاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Multiple gods working together would be more powerful and efficient.
Correction: Cooperation implies need and dependence. Each would be incapable alone, which contradicts the definition of God as all-powerful and self-sufficient.

Checkpoint
What are the two possibilities in this proof?
A) One god creates alone or both create together.
B) One god suffices or both are needed.
C) One god is strong or both are weak.
D) One god creates the world or none does.

Key Takeaway
The existence of two gods is impossible because either one would be redundant or both would be deficient.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficult situation, do you instinctively rely on Allah alone, or do you feel the need for other 'gods'—like money, status, or people—to make things happen? What does this passage say about that reliance?
?
If you truly believe that one God suffices for everything, why do you sometimes feel anxious as if you need multiple sources of support? What would it take for you to internalize the truth that Allah alone is enough?
?
The proof shows that needing another is a sign of incapacity. In your life, are there people or things that you feel you cannot live without? How would your life change if you acted on the belief that Allah's sufficiency eliminates all other needs?

Fourth Proof: Two Gods Cannot Create a Single Thing
Nasafi enumerates three scenarios to prove two gods cannot create a single thing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the existence of two gods leads to absurdity whether they create independently, cooperatively, or one alone.

Core Idea
One effect cannot have two complete causes, and a god cannot be dependent.

The author presents a crisp logical argument. He considers all possibilities for how two gods might create a single thing. Each possibility leads to a contradiction—either a logical impossibility or a failure of divinity. This proof decisively shows that tawhid (monotheism) is rationally necessary.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the original Arabic line even if you don't understand it. The density is intentional.
The Arabic uses key terms: استقلال (independence), تعاون (cooperation), عجز (incapacity).
2
Understand the three scenarios
The author examines three cases: independent creation, cooperative creation, and one alone. Identify each.
3
Analyze each case's logical flaw
For each, the author gives a reason why it fails. The independent case creates one effect from two causes. The cooperative case makes each dependent. The one-alone case shows the other is powerless.
This maps to the argument's structure.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The argument proves that multiple gods cannot coexist, because creation—already established as coming from Allah—cannot be attributed to two.
Connects to earlier proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعا: لو وجد إلهان وأرادا إيجاد شيء فإن أوجداه معا بالاستقلال بتمامه في وقت واحد لزم وجود أثر بين مؤثرين وهذا محال وإن أوجداه بالتعاون لزم احتياج كل منهما فلا يكون إلها وإن أوجده أحدهما فقد لزم عجز الآخر.
Fourth: If there were two gods and they willed to bring a thing into existence, then if they bring it into existence together, each independently completing it at one time, the existence of an effect between two causes would be necessary, and this is impossible. And if they bring it into existence through cooperation, each would be dependent on the other, so neither would be a god. And if one of them brings it into existence, then the other's incapacity necessarily follows.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This is the fourth proof, focusing on the creation of a single thing. If both gods act independently and each produces the entire thing at the same time, we would have one effect produced by two independent causes, which is absurd (a single effect cannot have two complete causes). If they cooperate, each produces only part, meaning each needs the other to complete the thing, so each is dependent—not divine. If only one creates it, the other is helpless. Thus, two gods cannot exist.

Key Terms
استقلال
تعاون
عجز
أثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Two gods could independently create the same thing if they agreed.
Correction: The argument shows that even if they agreed, one effect cannot have two complete causes; the existence of an effect from two causes is impossible in itself.

Checkpoint
What problem arises if two gods independently create the same thing?
A) They would disagree.
B) The thing would have two effects.
C) One effect would come from two causes, which is impossible.
D) The thing would be incomplete.

Key Takeaway
The existence of two gods is impossible because any scenario of their creating a single thing leads to an absurdity: either one effect from two causes, dependence, or incapacity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that any sharing of creation leads to absurdity, then in what areas of your life have you been acting as if someone or something else has independent power? Will you repent and reaffirm tawheed today?
?
The proof shows that a god cannot be dependent. How does this challenge your heart when you rely on created beings for what only Allah can give? What practical step will you take to shift your trust solely to Him?
?
Imagine standing before Allah knowing that attributing a partner to Him is the greatest injustice. If this logical proof solidifies in your mind, how must your du'a and hope change? Write one concrete change you will make in your worship this week.

Impossible Two Creators: The Argument from Power
Imam al-Nasafi proves the impossibility of two creators using the argument from power and answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the coexistence of two equal creators leads to absurdity, specifically through the argument from power, and how the author answers the objection from the single creator's case.

Core Idea
Two creators would incapacitate each other, which is impossible for the divine.

This passage presents a sophisticated argument against the possibility of two creators. It begins by stating a logical principle and then addresses a potential objection that might seem to undermine the reasoning. By distinguishing between voluntary cessation of power in a single creator and forced incapacitation in a supposed pair, Imam al-Nasafi clarifies why only one Creator can exist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial principle and conclusion
Read the first sentence: 'And the statement affirming two creators leads to this, and whatever leads to absurdity is absurd.' This sets up the logical framework.
The 'this' refers to the absurdity mentioned earlier in the text.
2
Understand the objection from the single creator's case
The author anticipates a counterexample: when a single creator originates movement, His power over rest ceases, but that is not incapacity. Why would it be different for two?
The objection tries to parallel the situation between one and two creators.
3
Analyze the author's distinction between voluntary and forced incapacitation
The author explains that the single creator's cessation is voluntary and due to the impossibility of combining opposites, while in two creators, it is forced by the other's action.
This distinction is key to rebutting the objection.
4
See how the distinction saves the argument
The single creator retains perfect power because He could have chosen the opposite; the two creators scenario implies coercion and subjugation, which is absurd for divine beings.
Thus, the proof stands: two creators cannot coexist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقول بثبوت صانعين يؤدي إلى هذا، وما أفضى إلى المحال فهو محال، ولا يقال: إن الواحد إذا أثبت فيه حركة زالت قدرته عن تخليق السكون فيه، ولم يكن ذلك تعجيزا لنفسه ولم يكن ذلك محالا، فكذا في الاثنين لأنا نقول: إن من زالت قدرته عن إثبات شيء في محل إثبات غيره ضد ذلك الشيء كان عاجزا بتعجيز غيره إياه عن إثبات ما كانت قدرته ثابتة عليه بإثبات عليه ذلك الغير ضده لأن هذا منه تصرف في المحل ليمنع صاحبه عن التصرف فيه وتعجيز غيره تارة يكون بمنعه عن تنفيذ قدرته بتصرفه في ذاته بإبطال قدرته وتارة يكون بفعل في محل تصرف بإثبات ضد ما يريد صاحبه إثباته فيه وإخراجه من أن يكون قابلا لتصرفه بإثبات ضد تصرفه فيه، فأما من أثبت تصرفا في محل مع قدرته على إثبات ضده فيه على طريق البدل لن يعد عاجزا عن التصرف فيه وإن زالت قدرته لاستحالة الجمع بين الضدين إذا كان هو الذي أثبت هذا الضد فيه باختياره مع قدرته على إثبات ضده على البدل بل هو آية كمال القدرة وعلاقة نفاذ المشيئة، فأما في الاثنين فذلك علامة العجز والقهر على ما قدرنا، والله الموفق.
And the statement affirming two creators leads to this, and whatever leads to absurdity is absurd. It cannot be said: if the single [creator] originates a movement in [a body], his power over creating rest in it ceases, and that is not incapacity for himself nor is it absurd, so too for the two [creators]. For we say: He whose power ceases to originate a thing in a locus where another originates its opposite is rendered incapable by the other's incapacitation of him from originating what his power was established upon, because that act from him is a dispossession of the locus to prevent his partner from dispossessing in it. And the incapacitation of another is sometimes by preventing him from executing his power through a disposition in his self by annulling his power, and sometimes by an act in the locus of disposition by originating the opposite of what his partner intends to originate therein, and removing it from being receptive to his disposition by originating the opposite of his disposition. As for one who originates a disposition in a locus while having power over originating its opposite in it by way of substitution, he is not considered incapable of disposition in it even if his power ceases, due to the impossibility of combining two opposites, since he himself originated this opposite in it by his own choice while having power over originating its opposite by substitution. Rather, that is a sign of perfection of power and relation of the execution of the will. As for two [creators], that is a sign of incapacity and subjugation, as we determined. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the impossibility of two creators, focusing on the concept of power (qudra). The author begins by stating the principle: claiming two creators leads to absurdity, and what leads to absurdity is absurd. He then anticipates an objection: when a single creator originates a movement, his power over creating rest in that same locus ceases, but this is not counted as incapacity for himself. So why would the same situation be absurd for two creators? The answer explains the key difference. In the single creator's case, the cessation of power over the opposite (rest) is due to the impossibility of simultaneously combining two opposites; he himself chose to originate movement, and he had the power to originate rest instead if he wished. This actually demonstrates the perfection of his power and the execution of his will. However, in the case of two creators, one originates an opposite in the locus, and the other's power over the opposite is forcibly removed by the action of the other. This is true incapacitation and subjugation, proving that two equal creators cannot coexist without one being subjugated, which is absurd. Thus, the objection fails, and the proof stands.

Key Terms
صانعين
المحال
القدرة
التعجيز
الضدان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the single creator's cessation of power over an opposite is a form of incapacity.
Correction: The author clarifies it is voluntary and a sign of perfect power, not weakness, because the creator could have chosen the opposite instead.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, why is the cessation of power over the opposite in the case of a single creator not considered incapacitation?
A) Because he is forced by an external agent.
B) Because he himself chose to originate one opposite while having the ability to originate the other instead.
C) Because he has no power over the opposite at all.
D) Because the opposite does not exist.

Key Takeaway
The coexistence of two equal creators is impossible because they would incapacitate each other, unlike the single Creator's voluntary acts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself torn between obeying Allah and following your own desires, do you realize that there can only be one true authority over your life? How does this proof that two creators cannot coexist challenge you to submit completely to His will?
?
The lesson shows that involuntary incapacitation is a sign of weakness. Is there a relationship, habit, or fear that has incapacitated you from obeying Allah fully? What would it look like to trust only in His power to free you?
?
The single Creator's cessation of power is voluntary—a sign of perfection. Are you willing to let go of your pride, control, or plans and surrender to Allah's choice, even when it means accepting what you didn't originally want? What is one specific area you need to surrender today?

Proof of Mutual Hindrance Based on Will
Al-Nasafi presents the proof of mutual hindrance using conflicting divine wills.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof of mutual hindrance (tamānu') that uses conflicting divine wills to demonstrate the necessity of a single Creator.

Core Idea
Conflicting wills cannot coexist; only one Creator's will can prevail.

Imam al-Nasafi presents a variation of the classic proof of mutual hindrance, focusing on divine will rather than power. By imagining two creators with opposite intentions, he shows that the only coherent outcome is that one creator's will must dominate, proving his divinity and nullifying the other's. This logical demonstration reinforces the Islamic doctrine of tawhid, affirming that there can only be one God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Try to grasp the scenario: two creators with conflicting wills.
Notice that the proof is based on will (irada), not power (qudra).
2
Identify the three logical possibilities
The passage lists three possible outcomes for two conflicting wills. Identify each one: both realized, neither realized, or only one realized.
The author uses 'either...or...' structure.
3
Understand why the first two are impossible
Think about why both wills being realized leads to contradictions (e.g., a person simultaneously alive and dead). Similarly, neither will being realized leaves no attributes at all.
These are logically impossible (muhāl).
4
Recognize the only coherent conclusion
The only possibility left is that one will prevails. This establishes the divinity of the one whose will is executed and nullifies the other's divinity.
Thus, there cannot be two equally powerful creators with opposing wills.
5
Connect to the Quranic basis
Note that the proof is derived from the Quranic verse about corruption if there were multiple gods. This shows the harmony between reason and revelation.
The verse is partially quoted at the end.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وربما عدى أهل الحق هذه الدلالة عن القدرة إلى الإرادة وقالوا: يقدر في الأوهام وقوع الاختلاف بين الصانعين لو كانا للعالم في الإرادة فيريد أحدهما إيجاد الحياة في شخص والآخر إيجاد الموت فيه، وكذا هذا في الحركة والسكون والسواد والبياض وجميع أنواع المتضادات. فبعد ذلك لا يخلو إما أن يحصل مرادهما جميعا فيصير الشخص الواحد في حالة واحدة حيا ميتا ساكنا متحركا أسود أبيض وهذا محال، وإما أن لا يحصل مرادهما فيبقى الشخص لا حيا ولا ميتا ولا ساكنا ولا متحركا وهذا محال، ويثبت عجز كل واحد منهما لتعطل إرادته وامتناع إثبات ما يريد إثباته بمنع صاحبه إياه إذ لولا إرادة صاحبه ضد مراده لحصل مراده ونفذت مشيئته، وفيه بطلان ربوبيتهما جميعا، وإما أن ينفذ مراد أحدهما دون الآخر وفيها ثبات ألوهية من نفذت إرادته وبطلان إلوهية الآخر وهذه الدلالة تسمى التمانع وأخذها المتكلمون من كلام الله. قال الله تعالى: ﴿ لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا
And sometimes the people of truth transferred this proof from power to will and said: It is conceivable in estimations that difference would occur between the two creators, if there were two for the world, in will. One wants to bring about life in a person, the other wants to bring about death in him. Similarly for movement and rest, black and white, and all types of opposites. Then, after that, it is unavoidable that either both of their wills are realized, so the single person becomes alive, dead, moving, still, black, white in one state—this is impossible. Or neither of their wills is realized, so the person remains not alive nor dead, not moving nor still—this is impossible, and the incapacity of each one is established due to the failure of his will and the impossibility of bringing about what he wants to bring about due to the prevention of his partner from him, for if not for his partner's will of the opposite of his will, his will would have been realized and his wish executed. In that is the nullity of the lordship of both. Or the will of one is executed without the other, and in that is the establishment of the divinity of the one whose will is executed and the nullity of the divinity of the other. And this proof is called 'al-tamānu'' (mutual hindrance), and the theologians took it from the speech of Allah. Allah says: 'If there were in them...'
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage presents the proof of mutual hindrance (tamānu'), which focuses on will (irada) rather than power. The author says that the people of truth (Ahl al-Haqq) sometimes use this proof. They ask the reader to imagine two creators of the world with conflicting wills—for example, one wants life for a person, the other wants death. This applies to all opposites like movement/rest, black/white. Then there are three logical possibilities. First, both wills are realized, resulting in the person being simultaneously alive and dead, moving and still, etc.—this is impossible (muhāl). Second, neither will is realized, leaving the person with no attributes—also impossible. In both cases, incapacity is proven for both, nullifying their divinity. Third, only one will is realized, which establishes the divinity of the one whose will prevails and nullifies the divinity of the other. Thus, the existence of two equally powerful creators with conflicting wills is absurd. The proof is called tamānu' because each would hinder the other's will. The author notes that the theologians derived this from the Quranic verse 'If there were in them gods besides Allah, they would have been corrupted' (Quran 21:22).

Key Terms
التمانع
الإرادة
الأوهام
المتضادات
الألوهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof of mutual hindrance is based solely on divine power (qudra), not will (irada).
Correction: This passage explicitly shows the proof can be based on will, using conflicting intentions to demonstrate absurdity.

Checkpoint
In the proof of mutual hindrance, what is the only coherent outcome when two creators have conflicting wills?
A) Both wills are realized simultaneously.
B) Neither will is realized.
C) One will is executed and the other is not.
D) The two creators compromise and create a third state.

Key Takeaway
The proof of mutual hindrance (tamānu') based on will demonstrates that only one Creator can exist, as conflicting wills lead to logical absurdity unless one prevails.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often act as if your plans and fears can override Allah's will. How does the logical absurdity of conflicting wills challenge you to surrender your own desires to His sole command? What one decision today will you consciously submit to His will alone?
?
The proof shows that if two wills conflict, only one can truly be divine. Consider the competing loyalties in your heart—your career, your relationships, your comfort. Which of those do you treat as a 'controlling will' alongside Allah? What would it mean to dethrone them and let His will reign unchallenged?
?
When you face a difficult situation, do you find yourself wishing for a different decree? This proof demonstrates that only one will can be effective. Are you willing to accept that whatever happens is the outcome of His sole will—and that your opposition to it is, in effect, a claim to equal authority? How will you respond to the next test with full trust in His wisdom?

Allah's Existence

The Tamānu' Argument: Conceptual Proof of Divine Oneness
Al-Nasafi presents the logical argument for the impossibility of two gods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the tamānu' argument and how it proves that only one God can exist.

Core Idea
Conflict in will between two gods leads to absurdity, proving only one God.

Al-Nasafi presents the mature formulation of the proof of mutual hindrance, which focuses on divine will rather than power. This argument is a cornerstone of kalām theology, demonstrating that the existence of two all-powerful beings is logically impossible. Let's delve into the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Understand the scenario
The argument begins by imagining two gods with conflicting wills. Notice that the conflict is in will (irāda), not just power.
2
Examine the three possibilities
List the three logical outcomes: both wills fulfilled, neither fulfilled, or only one fulfilled.
3
See why the first two are impossible
Both fulfilled leads to contradictions (e.g., alive and dead); neither fulfilled implies impotence.
4
Recognize the conclusion
Only one will can be fulfilled, which establishes the divinity of the successful god and nullifies the other.
5
Identify the name of the argument
This is called dalālat al-tamānu' (mutual hindrance).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وربما عدى أهل الحق هذه الدلالة عن القدرة إلى الإرادة وقالوا: يقدر في الأوهام وقوع الاختلاف بين الصانعين لو كانا للعالم في الإرادة فيريد أحدهما إيجاد الحياة في شخص والآخر إيجاد الموت فيه، وكذا هذا في الحركة والسكون والسواد والبياض وجميع أنواع المتضادات. فبعد ذلك لا يخلو إما أن يحصل مرادهما جميعا فيصير الشخص الواحد في حالة واحدة حيا ميتا ساكنا متحركا أسود أبيض وهذا محال، وإما أن لا يحصل مرادهما فيبقى الشخص لا حيا ولا ميتا ولا ساكنا ولا متحركا وهذا محال، ويثبت عجز كل واحد منهما لتعطل إرادته وامتناع إثبات ما يريد إثباته بمنع صاحبه إياه إذ لولا إرادة صاحبه ضد مراده لحصل مراده ونفذت مشيئته، وفيه بطلان ربوبيتهما جميعا، وإما أن ينفذ مراد أحدهما دون الآخر وفيها ثبات ألوهية من نفذت إرادته وبطلان إلوهية الآخر وهذه الدلالة تسمى التمانع وأخذها المتكلمون من كلام الله. قال الله تعالى: ﴿ لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا آلِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَتَا ﴾ وقال عز وجل: ﴿ لَعَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ ﴾ وقال الله تعالى في إبطال إلوهية من اعتقدت عبدة الأصنام ألوهيته: ﴿ وَإِن يَمْسَسْكَ اللَّهُ بِضُرٍ فَلَا كَاشِفَ لَهُ إِلَّا هُوَ وَإِن يَمْسَسْكَ بِخَيْرٍ فَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ ﴾ أي أن يمسسك بخير فلا دافع له إلا هو إلا أنه اكتفى بذكره في الأول عن الإعادة في الثاني إيثارا للاختصار كما قال عز وجل في آية أخرى: ﴿ وَالْحَافِظِينَ فُرُوجَهُمْ وَالْحَافِظَاتِ ﴾ فكان فيه إثبات ألوهيته لنفاذ مشيئة، والاستدلال على كمال قدرته بذلك على ما قال ﴿ فَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ ﴾ وإبطال ربوبية غيره بعجزه عن كشف ما أثبته الله تعالى، وقال في آية أخرى: ﴿ وَإِن يَمْسَسْكَ اللَّهُ بِضُرٍ فَلَا كَاشِفَ لَهُ إِلَّا هُوَ وَإِن يُرِدْكَ بِخَيْرٍ فَلَا رَادَّ لِفَضْلِهِ ﴾ وقال في آية أخرى: ﴿ قُلْ أَفَرَأَيْتُم مَّا تَدْعُونَ مِن دُونِ اللَّهِ إِنْ أَرَادَنِيَ اللَّهُ بِضُرٍ هَلْ هُنَّ كَاشِفَاتُ ضُرِّهِ أَوْ أَرَادَنِي بِرَحْمَةٍ هَلْ هُنَّ مُمْسِكَاتُ رَحْمَتِهِ ﴾ ووجه الاستدلال على ما مر. وقال عز وجل في آية أخرى: ﴿ قُلْ أَرَأَيْتُمْ إِنْ أَخَذَ اللَّهُ سَمْعَكُمْ وَأَبْصَارَكُمْ وَخَتَمَ عَلَى قُلُوبِكُم مَّنْ إِلَهٌ غَيْرُ اللَّهِ يَأْتِيكُم بِهِ ﴾ استدل بانعدام أم القدرة لغيره على الإتيان بهذه الأشياء عند أخذه إياها على وحدانيته واستحالة ألوهية من لا قدرة له على ذلك. وهذه الدلالة لا تستقيم على أصول المعتزلة فإنهم يقولون: إن الله تعالى أراد من كل كافر الإيمان وأراد الكافر من نفسه الكفر، فنفذت إرادة الكافر وتعطلت إرادة الله ولم تبطل ربوبيته، ولم تزل أوائل المعتزلة كانوا يرومون التخلص عن هذا الإلزام بحيل.
And perhaps the people of truth transferred this indication from power to will and said: It is conceivable in imaginations that disagreement occurs between the two makers if there were for the world two makers in will, so one of them wills to bring life to a person and the other wills to bring death to him, and likewise in movement and stillness, blackness and whiteness, and all types of opposites. Then after that, it is inevitable that either both of their wills are fulfilled, so the single person becomes in one state alive, dead, still, moving, black, white — and this is impossible; or their wills are not fulfilled, so the person remains neither alive nor dead, neither still nor moving — and this is impossible, and the incapacity of each of them is established due to the failure of his will and the impossibility of establishing what he wishes to establish by his companion's prevention of him, for were it not for his companion's will opposing his will, his will would have been fulfilled and his wish would have been executed — and in this is the nullification of the lordship of both of them; or the will of one of them is executed without the other — and in this is the establishment of the divinity of the one whose will is executed and the nullification of the divinity of the other. And this indication is called al-tamānu' (mutual hindrance), and the theologians (mutakallimūn) took it from the speech of Allah. Allah the Most High said: 'If there had been gods in them besides Allah, they would have been corrupted.' And He, exalted and majestic, said: 'Then each would have overcome the other.' And Allah the Most High said, in refuting the divinity of those whose divinity the idol worshippers believed: 'And if Allah touches you with harm, there is no remover of it except Him, and if He touches you with good, then He is over all things competent.' Meaning that if He touches you with good, there is no repeller of it except Him, but He sufficed with its mention in the first instance and did not repeat it in the second, preferring brevity, just as He, exalted and majestic, said in another verse: 'And the men who guard their private parts and the women who guard.' So in it is the establishment of His divinity (ulūhiyya) through the execution of His will, and the inference of the perfection of His power by that, as He said: 'He is over all things competent.' And the nullification of the lordship of other than Him due to its inability to remove what Allah has established. And He said in another verse: 'And if Allah touches you with harm, there is no remover of it except Him, and if He intends for you good, there is no repeller of His bounty.' And He said in another verse: 'Say: Do you see what you call upon besides Allah? If Allah intends harm for me, can they remove His harm? Or if He intends me mercy, can they withhold His mercy?' And the manner of inference is as previously mentioned. And He, exalted and majestic, said in another verse: 'Say: Have you considered if Allah took away your hearing and your sight and sealed your hearts, which god other than Allah could bring them back to you?' He inferred from the absence of the power of other than Him to bring these things when He takes them, regarding His oneness and the impossibility of the divinity of one who has no power over that. And this indication does not stand on the principles of the Mu'tazila, for they say: Allah the Most High willed faith from every disbeliever, and the disbeliever willed from himself disbelief, so the will of the disbeliever was executed and the will of Allah was frustrated, yet His lordship was not nullified. And the early Mu'tazila continued to try to extricate themselves from this necessary implication by tricks.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage presents the classical kalām proof known as dalālat al-tamānu' (the proof of mutual hindrance) and then provides Qur'anic evidence for it, concluding with a note that this proof does not hold on Mu'tazilite principles. The author begins by noting that the 'people of truth' (Ahl al-Haqq) shifted the basis of this argument from divine power (qudra) to divine will (irāda). The argument runs as follows: if there were two creators of the universe, we can conceive a situation where their wills conflict—one wants to give life to a person, the other wants to cause death; similarly for motion versus stillness, black versus white, and all pairs of opposites. Then there are three possibilities: (1) Both wills are fulfilled, which would mean a single person is simultaneously alive and dead, moving and still, black and white—an impossibility. (2) Neither will is fulfilled, leaving the person neither alive nor dead, etc.—also impossible. This shows that each god would be incapable of carrying out his will because the other prevents him, which invalidates the lordship (rubūbiyya) of both. (3) The will of one is fulfilled and the other is not; this establishes the divinity (ulūhiyya) of the successful one and nullifies the other. The author then states that this is called al-tamānu' and that theologians derived it from the Qur'an. He cites several verses: Quran 21:22 (if there were gods besides Allah, heavens and earth would be corrupted), Quran 23:91 (gods would overcome each other), Quran 6:17 (no one can remove harm or repel good except Allah), and others. He explains how these verses show that only the true God has full power and execution of will, and that anything else lacks such power, proving the impossibility of multiple gods. Finally, the author notes that this proof does not hold on the principles of the Mu'tazila, because they accept that God can will something and yet it does not happen—e.g., He wills faith from a disbeliever, but the disbeliever chooses disbelief and God's will is frustrated. This would allow for the possibility of two gods conflicting wills without either being invalidated. The early Mu'tazila tried to evade this implication with various tricks, but the author does not elaborate further.

Key Terms
دلالة التمانع
التمانع
الإرادة
المتضادات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The tamānu' argument only works if two gods compete in power (qudra).
Correction: The mature formulation focuses on will (irāda), because conflict in will is more fundamental and avoids issues of divine attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the tamānu' argument, which of the following is NOT one of the three possibilities when two gods have conflicting wills?
A) Both wills are fulfilled.
B) Neither will is fulfilled.
C) The gods compromise and merge their wills.
D) Only one will is fulfilled.

Key Takeaway
The tamānu' argument uses the logical impossibility of conflicting divine wills to prove that there can be only one true God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face conflicting desires in your heart—two ambitions pulling you in opposite directions—do you recognize that only one ultimate Will (Allah’s) can bring true harmony? How does this lesson push you to surrender your competing goals to His oneness today?
?
The tamānu' argument shows that a world with two gods would be logically impossible. Have you ever behaved as if you were a 'co-ruler' with Allah, trying to control areas of your life that only He can manage? What concrete step can you take this week to hand that control back to Him?
?
If you truly internalized that only one God can exist, and that His will alone prevails, how would it change the way you pray, plan, and respond to disappointment? What is one thing you can do right now to align your heart with this truth?
