Quranic Evidence for the Tamānu' Argument
Al-Nasafi cites Qur'anic verses as evidence for the tamānu' argument and explains their significance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will recognize how Qur'anic verses are used as evidence for the tamānu' argument and how they demonstrate that only Allah has full control over harm and benefit.

Core Idea
The Qur'an confirms that no god besides Allah can remove harm or grant good, proving His exclusive divinity.

Al-Nasafi now shows that the tamānu' argument is not merely a rational construct but is rooted in the Qur'an. He cites several verses that emphasize Allah's exclusive power to bring harm and benefit, and His ability to take away senses and restore them. These verses refute the divinity of any other being and support the logical proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses cited
Notice the verses from Surah al-Anbiya (21:22), al-Mu'minun (23:91), al-An'am (6:17), and others.
2
Understand the inference
Each verse points to the impossibility of another god having power over harm or good.
3
See the connection to the argument
The verses show that only one being can execute will without hindrance, which is the conclusion of tamānu'.
4
Note the exegetical style
Al-Nasafi explains that the verse about good is implicit (brevity).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وربما عدى أهل الحق هذه الدلالة عن القدرة إلى الإرادة وقالوا: يقدر في الأوهام وقوع الاختلاف بين الصانعين لو كانا للعالم في الإرادة فيريد أحدهما إيجاد الحياة في شخص والآخر إيجاد الموت فيه، وكذا هذا في الحركة والسكون والسواد والبياض وجميع أنواع المتضادات. فبعد ذلك لا يخلو إما أن يحصل مرادهما جميعا فيصير الشخص الواحد في حالة واحدة حيا ميتا ساكنا متحركا أسود أبيض وهذا محال، وإما أن لا يحصل مرادهما فيبقى الشخص لا حيا ولا ميتا ولا ساكنا ولا متحركا وهذا محال، ويثبت عجز كل واحد منهما لتعطل إرادته وامتناع إثبات ما يريد إثباته بمنع صاحبه إياه إذ لولا إرادة صاحبه ضد مراده لحصل مراده ونفذت مشيئته، وفيه بطلان ربوبيتهما جميعا، وإما أن ينفذ مراد أحدهما دون الآخر وفيها ثبات ألوهية من نفذت إرادته وبطلان إلوهية الآخر وهذه الدلالة تسمى التمانع وأخذها المتكلمون من كلام الله. قال الله تعالى: ﴿ لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا آلِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَتَا ﴾ وقال عز وجل: ﴿ لَعَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ ﴾ وقال الله تعالى في إبطال إلوهية من اعتقدت عبدة الأصنام ألوهيته: ﴿ وَإِن يَمْسَسْكَ اللَّهُ بِضُرٍ فَلَا كَاشِفَ لَهُ إِلَّا هُوَ وَإِن يَمْسَسْكَ بِخَيْرٍ فَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ ﴾ أي أن يمسسك بخير فلا دافع له إلا هو إلا أنه اكتفى بذكره في الأول عن الإعادة في الثاني إيثارا للاختصار كما قال عز وجل في آية أخرى: ﴿ وَالْحَافِظِينَ فُرُوجَهُمْ وَالْحَافِظَاتِ ﴾ فكان فيه إثبات ألوهيته لنفاذ مشيئة، والاستدلال على كمال قدرته بذلك على ما قال ﴿ فَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ ﴾ وإبطال ربوبية غيره بعجزه عن كشف ما أثبته الله تعالى، وقال في آية أخرى: ﴿ وَإِن يَمْسَسْكَ اللَّهُ بِضُرٍ فَلَا كَاشِفَ لَهُ إِلَّا هُوَ وَإِن يُرِدْكَ بِخَيْرٍ فَلَا رَادَّ لِفَضْلِهِ ﴾ وقال في آية أخرى: ﴿ قُلْ أَفَرَأَيْتُم مَّا تَدْعُونَ مِن دُونِ اللَّهِ إِنْ أَرَادَنِيَ اللَّهُ بِضُرٍ هَلْ هُنَّ كَاشِفَاتُ ضُرِّهِ أَوْ أَرَادَنِي بِرَحْمَةٍ هَلْ هُنَّ مُمْسِكَاتُ رَحْمَتِهِ ﴾ ووجه الاستدلال على ما مر. وقال عز وجل في آية أخرى: ﴿ قُلْ أَرَأَيْتُمْ إِنْ أَخَذَ اللَّهُ سَمْعَكُمْ وَأَبْصَارَكُمْ وَخَتَمَ عَلَى قُلُوبِكُم مَّنْ إِلَهٌ غَيْرُ اللَّهِ يَأْتِيكُم بِهِ ﴾ استدل بانعدام أم القدرة لغيره على الإتيان بهذه الأشياء عند أخذه إياها على وحدانيته واستحالة ألوهية من لا قدرة له على ذلك. وهذه الدلالة لا تستقيم على أصول المعتزلة فإنهم يقولون: إن الله تعالى أراد من كل كافر الإيمان وأراد الكافر من نفسه الكفر، فنفذت إرادة الكافر وتعطلت إرادة الله ولم تبطل ربوبيته، ولم تزل أوائل المعتزلة كانوا يرومون التخلص عن هذا الإلزام بحيل.
And perhaps the people of truth transferred this indication from power to will and said: It is conceivable in imaginations that disagreement occurs between the two makers if there were for the world two makers in will, so one of them wills to bring life to a person and the other wills to bring death to him, and likewise in movement and stillness, blackness and whiteness, and all types of opposites. Then after that, it is inevitable that either both of their wills are fulfilled, so the single person becomes in one state alive, dead, still, moving, black, white — and this is impossible; or their wills are not fulfilled, so the person remains neither alive nor dead, neither still nor moving — and this is impossible, and the incapacity of each of them is established due to the failure of his will and the impossibility of establishing what he wishes to establish by his companion's prevention of him, for were it not for his companion's will opposing his will, his will would have been fulfilled and his wish would have been executed — and in this is the nullification of the lordship of both of them; or the will of one of them is executed without the other — and in this is the establishment of the divinity of the one whose will is executed and the nullification of the divinity of the other. And this indication is called al-tamānu' (mutual hindrance), and the theologians (mutakallimūn) took it from the speech of Allah. Allah the Most High said: 'If there had been gods in them besides Allah, they would have been corrupted.' And He, exalted and majestic, said: 'Then each would have overcome the other.' And Allah the Most High said, in refuting the divinity of those whose divinity the idol worshippers believed: 'And if Allah touches you with harm, there is no remover of it except Him, and if He touches you with good, then He is over all things competent.' Meaning that if He touches you with good, there is no repeller of it except Him, but He sufficed with its mention in the first instance and did not repeat it in the second, preferring brevity, just as He, exalted and majestic, said in another verse: 'And the men who guard their private parts and the women who guard.' So in it is the establishment of His divinity (ulūhiyya) through the execution of His will, and the inference of the perfection of His power by that, as He said: 'He is over all things competent.' And the nullification of the lordship of other than Him due to its inability to remove what Allah has established. And He said in another verse: 'And if Allah touches you with harm, there is no remover of it except Him, and if He intends for you good, there is no repeller of His bounty.' And He said in another verse: 'Say: Do you see what you call upon besides Allah? If Allah intends harm for me, can they remove His harm? Or if He intends me mercy, can they withhold His mercy?' And the manner of inference is as previously mentioned. And He, exalted and majestic, said in another verse: 'Say: Have you considered if Allah took away your hearing and your sight and sealed your hearts, which god other than Allah could bring them back to you?' He inferred from the absence of the power of other than Him to bring these things when He takes them, regarding His oneness and the impossibility of the divinity of one who has no power over that. And this indication does not stand on the principles of the Mu'tazila, for they say: Allah the Most High willed faith from every disbeliever, and the disbeliever willed from himself disbelief, so the will of the disbeliever was executed and the will of Allah was frustrated, yet His lordship was not nullified. And the early Mu'tazila continued to try to extricate themselves from this necessary implication by tricks.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage presents the classical kalām proof known as dalālat al-tamānu' (the proof of mutual hindrance) and then provides Qur'anic evidence for it, concluding with a note that this proof does not hold on Mu'tazilite principles. The author begins by noting that the 'people of truth' (Ahl al-Haqq) shifted the basis of this argument from divine power (qudra) to divine will (irāda). The argument runs as follows: if there were two creators of the universe, we can conceive a situation where their wills conflict—one wants to give life to a person, the other wants to cause death; similarly for motion versus stillness, black versus white, and all pairs of opposites. Then there are three possibilities: (1) Both wills are fulfilled, which would mean a single person is simultaneously alive and dead, moving and still, black and white—an impossibility. (2) Neither will is fulfilled, leaving the person neither alive nor dead, etc.—also impossible. This shows that each god would be incapable of carrying out his will because the other prevents him, which invalidates the lordship (rubūbiyya) of both. (3) The will of one is fulfilled and the other is not; this establishes the divinity (ulūhiyya) of the successful one and nullifies the other. The author then states that this is called al-tamānu' and that theologians derived it from the Qur'an. He cites several verses: Quran 21:22 (if there were gods besides Allah, heavens and earth would be corrupted), Quran 23:91 (gods would overcome each other), Quran 6:17 (no one can remove harm or repel good except Allah), and others. He explains how these verses show that only the true God has full power and execution of will, and that anything else lacks such power, proving the impossibility of multiple gods. Finally, the author notes that this proof does not hold on the principles of the Mu'tazila, because they accept that God can will something and yet it does not happen—e.g., He wills faith from a disbeliever, but the disbeliever chooses disbelief and God's will is frustrated. This would allow for the possibility of two gods conflicting wills without either being invalidated. The early Mu'tazila tried to evade this implication with various tricks, but the author does not elaborate further.

التمانس

A) 23:91
B) 21:22
C) 6:17
D) 10:107

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an provides direct evidence for the tamānu' argument by asserting that only Allah has uncompromised power over harm and benefit.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficulty, do your heart's hopes turn to a doctor, a friend, or a plan more than to Allah? How does the verse 'If Allah touches you with harm, none can remove it except Him' challenge your actual trust? Will you today consciously redirect your reliance to Allah alone?
?
The tamānu' argument proves that if there were multiple gods, chaos would result. In your own life, have you ever served two masters—seeking approval from people while claiming to worship Allah? How does this logical proof expose the inconsistency? What will you do to make your worship exclusive?
?
Allah alone has the power to grant good and repel harm. Think of a recent desire you had—did you ask Allah for it, or did you rely on your own effort? What does your prayer life reveal about your belief in this verse? Commit to asking Allah for everything, big and small, starting today.

Allah's Existence
intermediate

Why the Tamānu' Argument Fails on Mu'tazilite Principles
Al-Nasafi explains why the tamānu' argument does not work on Mu'tazilite principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the tamānu' argument does not hold according to Mu'tazilite theology, due to their belief that God's will can be frustrated by human free will.

Core Idea
Mu'tazila allow that God's will can be thwarted, so the tamānu' argument's conclusion does not apply.

Al-Nasafi concludes by noting a critical limitation: the tamānu' argument is not valid on Mu'tazilite principles. The Mu'tazila believe that God wills faith from every disbeliever, but the disbeliever can choose disbelief, and God's will is not fulfilled. This would allow a scenario where two gods have conflicting wills without either being invalidated. The author notes that early Mu'tazila attempted to evade this implication through various tricks.

Guided Path
1
Understand Mu'tazilite view on will
They hold that God wills the good (faith) from every human, but humans have free will to oppose.
2
Apply to the tamānu' scenario
In a two-god scenario, one god could will life and the other will death, and the person's free choice could break the tie, so the argument's impossibility does not follow.
3
Recognize the implication
For Mu'tazila, the tamānu' argument does not prove tawḥīd, because they accept that God's will can be frustrated.
4
Note the historical response
Early Mu'tazila tried to find ways around this objection.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وربما عدى أهل الحق هذه الدلالة عن القدرة إلى الإرادة وقالوا: يقدر في الأوهام وقوع الاختلاف بين الصانعين لو كانا للعالم في الإرادة فيريد أحدهما إيجاد الحياة في شخص والآخر إيجاد الموت فيه، وكذا هذا في الحركة والسكون والسواد والبياض وجميع أنواع المتضادات. فبعد ذلك لا يخلو إما أن يحصل مرادهما جميعا فيصير الشخص الواحد في حالة واحدة حيا ميتا ساكنا متحركا أسود أبيض وهذا محال، وإما أن لا يحصل مرادهما فيبقى الشخص لا حيا ولا ميتا ولا ساكنا ولا متحركا وهذا محال، ويثبت عجز كل واحد منهما لتعطل إرادته وامتناع إثبات ما يريد إثباته بمنع صاحبه إياه إذ لولا إرادة صاحبه ضد مراده لحصل مراده ونفذت مشيئته، وفيه بطلان ربوبيتهما جميعا، وإما أن ينفذ مراد أحدهما دون الآخر وفيها ثبات ألوهية من نفذت إرادته وبطلان إلوهية الآخر وهذه الدلالة تسمى التمانع وأخذها المتكلمون من كلام الله. قال الله تعالى: ﴿ لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا آلِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَتَا ﴾ وقال عز وجل: ﴿ لَعَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ ﴾ وقال الله تعالى في إبطال إلوهية من اعتقدت عبدة الأصنام ألوهيته: ﴿ وَإِن يَمْسَسْكَ اللَّهُ بِضُرٍ فَلَا كَاشِفَ لَهُ إِلَّا هُوَ وَإِن يَمْسَسْكَ بِخَيْرٍ فَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ ﴾ أي أن يمسسك بخير فلا دافع له إلا هو إلا أنه اكتفى بذكره في الأول عن الإعادة في الثاني إيثارا للاختصار كما قال عز وجل في آية أخرى: ﴿ وَالْحَافِظِينَ فُرُوجَهُمْ وَالْحَافِظَاتِ ﴾ فكان فيه إثبات ألوهيته لنفاذ مشيئة، والاستدلال على كمال قدرته بذلك على ما قال ﴿ فَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ ﴾ وإبطال ربوبية غيره بعجزه عن كشف ما أثبته الله تعالى، وقال في آية أخرى: ﴿ وَإِن يَمْسَسْكَ اللَّهُ بِضُرٍ فَلَا كَاشِفَ لَهُ إِلَّا هُوَ وَإِن يُرِدْكَ بِخَيْرٍ فَلَا رَادَّ لِفَضْلِهِ ﴾ وقال في آية أخرى: ﴿ قُلْ أَفَرَأَيْتُم مَّا تَدْعُونَ مِن دُونِ اللَّهِ إِنْ أَرَادَنِيَ اللَّهُ بِضُرٍ هَلْ هُنَّ كَاشِفَاتُ ضُرِّهِ أَوْ أَرَادَنِي بِرَحْمَةٍ هَلْ هُنَّ مُمْسِكَاتُ رَحْمَتِهِ ﴾ ووجه الاستدلال على ما مر. وقال عز وجل في آية أخرى: ﴿ قُلْ أَرَأَيْتُمْ إِنْ أَخَذَ اللَّهُ سَمْعَكُمْ وَأَبْصَارَكُمْ وَخَتَمَ عَلَى قُلُوبِكُم مَّنْ إِلَهٌ غَيْرُ اللَّهِ يَأْتِيكُم بِهِ ﴾ استدل بانعدام أم القدرة لغيره على Commentary

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The tamānu' argument is universally accepted in Islamic theology.
Correction: The Mu'tazila reject its validity because they believe God's will can be frustrated by human free will.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, why does the tamānu' argument not stand on Mu'tazilite principles?
A) They deny the existence of God's will.
B) They believe God's will can be frustrated.
C) They reject the concept of mutual hindrance.
D) They accept multiple gods.

Key Takeaway
The tamānu' argument's validity depends on a theological commitment that divine will is always effective, which Mu'tazila reject.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever acted as if your own will can override God's will, even while professing belief in His power? How does the Mu'tazilite concession here challenge your own assumptions about divine sovereignty?
?
If you were pressed to defend God's omnipotence against the reality of unfulfilled desires in the world, would you resort to 'tricks' like the early Mu'tazila? What is the cost of such intellectual evasions for your faith?
?
Reflecting on this lesson, do you find yourself more drawn to a theology where God's will is always effective or one where human freedom can frustrate it? Be honest: which view makes you more accountable for your choices?

Quranic Proofs for Divine Oneness
Imam al-Nasafi enumerates Quranic verses demonstrating Allah's exclusive power, proving His oneness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Nasafi uses Quranic verses to establish that only Allah can remove harm and grant good, thereby proving His oneness and the falsehood of other gods.

Core Idea
The Quran proves God's oneness by showing that only He can act independently.

Imam al-Nasafi begins by citing several Quranic verses that highlight the exclusive power of Allah. These verses form the basis of a rational argument for tawheed, showing that any being unable to remove harm or grant good cannot be a true deity.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses carefully
Read the Arabic passage containing multiple Quranic verses. Notice how each verse emphasizes that only Allah can remove harm, grant good, or restore senses.
Pay attention to the repeated structure: 'if Allah touches you with harm, none can remove it except Him'.
2
Identify the logical inference
Al-Nasafi explains that the verses prove Allah's sole divinity because effective will and perfect power belong exclusively to Him. Any being that cannot act independently cannot be a god.
The inference is that inability to act proves false divinity.
3
Reflect on the cumulative proof
Consider how multiple verses reinforce the same point: from cosmic order to personal harm and good, all control belongs to Allah alone.
This shows the Quranic method of establishing tawheed.

ولو كان فيهما آلهة إلا الله لفسدنا وقال عز وجل ولعلا بعضهم على بعض وقال الله تعالى في إبطال إلوهية من اعتقدت عبدة الأصنام ألوهيته: وَإِن يَمْسَسْكَ اللَّهُ بِضُرٍ فَلَا كَاشِفَ لَهُ إِلَّا هُوَ وَإِن يَمْسَسْكَ بِخَيْرٍ فَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ أي أن يمسسك بخير فلا دافع له إلا هو إلا أنه اكتفى بذكره في الأول عن الإعادة في الثاني إيثارا للاختصار كما قال عز وجل في آية أخرى وَالْحَافِظِينَ فُرُوجَهُمْ وَالْحَافِظَاتِ فكان فيه إثبات ألوهيته لنفاذ مشيئته والاستدلال على كمال قدرته بذلك على ما قال فَهُوَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ وإبطال ربوبية غيره بعجزه عن كشف ما أثبته الله تعالى وقال في آية أخرى: وَإِن يَمْسَسْكَ اللَّهُ بِضُرٍ فَلَا كَاشِفَ لَهُ إِلَّا هُوَ وَإِن يُرِدْكَ بِخَيْرٍ فَلَا رَادَّ لِفَضْلِهِ وقال في آية أخرى: قُلْ أَفَرَأَيْتُم مَّا تَدْعُونَ مِن دُونِ اللَّهِ إِنْ أَرَادَنِيَ اللَّهُ بِضُرٍ هَلْ هُنَّ كَاشِفَاتُ ضُرِّهِ أَوْ أَرَادَنِي بِرَحْمَةٍ هَلْ هُنَّ مُمْسِكَاتُ رَحْمَتِهِ ووجه الاستدلال على ما مر وقال عز وجل في آية أخرى: قُلْ أَرَأَيْتُمْ إِنْ أَخَذَ اللَّهُ سَمْعَكُمْ وَأَبْصَارَكُمْ وَخَتَمَ عَلَى قُلُوبِكُم مَّنْ إِلَهُ غَيْرُ اللَّهِ يَأْتِيكُم بِهِ استدل بانعدام القدرة لغيره على الإتيان بهذه الأشياء عند أخذه إياها على وحدانيته واستحالة ألوهية من لا قدرة له على ذلك. وهذه الدلالة لا تستقيم على أصول المعتزلة فإنهم يقولون: إن الله تعالى أراد من كل كافر الإيمان وأراد الكافر من نفسه الكفر، فنفذت إرادة الكافر وتعطلت إرادة الله ولم تبطل ربوبيته، ولم تزل أوائل المعتزلة كانوا يرومون التخلص عن هذا الإلزام بحيل ضعيفة فلم يتمكنوا منه فالتزموا العجز عن إثبات الوحدانية بهذه الطرق التي علم الله تعالى نبيه وأمينه على وحيه المبعوث لإظهار الحق عند دروس آثاره وطموس أعلامه ومناره.
And if there were in them gods besides Allah, they would have been corrupted. And He, exalted, said: 'And some of them would have dominated others.' And Allah, exalted, said in nullifying the divinity of those whose divinity the idolaters believed: 'And if Allah touches you with harm, there is no remover of it except Him, and if He touches you with good, then He is over all things competent.' Meaning that if He touches you with good, there is no repeller of it except Him, except that He sufficed with mentioning it in the first [case] over repeating it in the second, preferring brevity, as He, exalted, said in another verse: 'And the men who guard their private parts and the women who guard.' So in it is the affirmation of His divinity due to the effectiveness of His will, and the inference to the perfection of His power by that, as He said: 'Then He is over all things competent.' And the nullification of the lordship of other than Him by its inability to remove what Allah has established. And He said in another verse: 'And if Allah touches you with harm, there is no remover of it except Him, and if He intends you with good, there is no repeller of His bounty.' And He said in another verse: 'Say: Have you considered what you invoke besides Allah? If Allah intends me with harm, are they removers of His harm? Or if He intends me with mercy, are they restrainers of His mercy?' And the manner of inference is as previously. And He, exalted, said in another verse: 'Say: Have you considered if Allah takes away your hearing and your sight and seals your hearts, which god other than Allah could bring them to you?' He inferred by the absence of power in other than Him to bring these things when He takes them [away], upon His oneness and the impossibility of divinity for one who has no power over that. And this proof is not valid according to the principles of the Mu'tazila, for they say: Allah, exalted, willed faith from every disbeliever, and the disbeliever willed disbelief from himself; so the will of the disbeliever was effective and the will of Allah was ineffective, yet His lordship is not nullified. And the early Mu'tazila used to seek to escape from this obligation by weak tricks, but they could not, so they committed themselves to inability to prove oneness by these methods which Allah, exalted, taught His Prophet and His trusted one over His revelation, sent to manifest the truth at the fading of His traces and the effacement of His signs and minaret.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a combined presentation of Quranic proofs for God's oneness (tawheed) and a critique of the Mu'tazila's inability to employ them due to their own theological principles. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, first quotes several Quranic verses that demonstrate that no one other than Allah can remove harm or grant good, thereby establishing His sole divinity and power. He then explains the inference: since only Allah can act in this way, any claimed deity must be powerless and false. However, al-Nasafi points out that this reasoning does not hold according to Mu'tazili principles because they believe that human will is effective and can contradict divine will. For example, a disbeliever's will to disbelieve can override Allah's will for him to believe, yet Allah's lordship remains intact. The Mu'tazila attempted to evade this inconsistency with weak arguments but eventually admitted their inability to prove oneness through these verses. Al-Nasafi thus shows that the Mu'tazili position undermines the very proofs they might use.

Key Terms
توحيد
إرادة
الألوهية
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think these verses only prove God's power over harm and good, but they actually prove that no other being has any independent power at all.
Correction: Al-Nasafi explicitly states that the inability of others to act proves the impossibility of their divinity, not just limited power.

Checkpoint
What common theme do all the verses cited by al-Nasafi share?
A) They emphasize that Allah can do anything He wills.
B) They state that only Allah has the power to harm or benefit.
C) They highlight that no one other than Allah can remove harm, grant good, or restore senses.
D) They argue that multiple gods would cause corruption.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Nasafi uses multiple Quranic verses to demonstrate that only Allah possesses effective will and perfect power, thereby establishing the logical necessity of tawheed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial, do you instinctively turn to people or solutions as if they have independent power to help you? How does the verse 'فَلَا كَاشِفَ لَهُ إِلَّا هُوَ' challenge that habit, and what concrete step will you take today to redirect your trust exclusively to Allah?
?
If Allah were to strip you of your hearing, sight, and understanding, could anyone return them to you? This absolute dependence is meant to strip your heart of pride. What is one area of your life where you still feel self-sufficient, and how will you surrender it to Allah in prayer this week?
?
You have just read clear verses proving that no other being has true power. Yet your actions often contradict this – you fear people more than Allah, or you cling to money as if it provides security. Which of these 'hidden gods' is hardest for you to abandon, and what is the first step you will take to dethrone it, starting today?

Mu'tazili Inconsistency with the Quranic Proofs
Imam al-Nasafi critiques the Mu'tazili inability to use Quranic proofs due to their doctrine of effective human will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazili belief in effective human will prevents them from using the Quranic proofs for tawheed and the historical conclusion of their inability.

Core Idea
Mu'tazili theology makes the Quranic proofs for God's oneness unworkable.

After presenting the Quranic proofs, Imam al-Nasafi points out a critical inconsistency: the Mu'tazila cannot validly use these verses because their own principles allow human will to override divine will. Thus, they end up unable to prove tawheed through these clear proofs.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazili position
Al-Nasafi states that the Mu'tazila believe Allah wills faith from every disbeliever, but the disbeliever wills disbelief, and the disbeliever's will is effective. This means human will can contradict and override divine will.
This is a key difference from Sunni theology where divine will is always effective.
2
See the consequence for the proofs
If human will can be effective against Allah's will, then the exclusive power of Allah over harm and good is undermined. The verses that show only Allah can act would not prove His oneness on Mu'tazili grounds, because others' wills could theoretically be effective.
This is the logical flaw al-Nasafi exposes.
3
Learn the historical outcome
The early Mu'tazila tried to escape this problem with weak tricks but failed, eventually admitting their inability to prove tawheed through these Quranic methods.
This shows the consistency of the Sunni position.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Refuting the Mu'tazili Argument from Two Creators
Al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazili claim that two gods lead to contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazili argument against two creators is logically flawed and how al-Nasafi's refutation defends the possibility of multiple eternal creators.

Core Idea
Two creators do not lead to contradiction; the Mu'tazili reasoning confuses potential with actual.

Imam al-Nasafi addresses a key objection from the Mu'tazila who argue that multiple eternal creators are impossible due to logical conflict. He systematically dismantles their argument by showing that their inference misapplies the concept of power and inaction. In this lesson, we will examine the argument and its refutation, including an insightful analogy.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazili argument
First, read the passage carefully, noting the Mu'tazili claim that two creators would lead to a contradiction (existing and non-existing simultaneously).
The argument relies on the idea that each creator has power over the same object.
2
Identify the flawed premise
Ask yourself: what is the key assumption that makes the Mu'tazili argument seem valid? Notice it assumes that the second creator's inaction directly causes non-existence.
3
Understand al-Nasafi's refutation
Study how al-Nasafi refutes the argument: he explains that if one creator brings something into existence, it exists; the other's inaction does not negate that existence. Then, see how the analogy of two men moving a log illustrates the point.
The analogy shows that one mover acting suffices to move the log; the other's lack of action does not make it unmoved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتمسكوا بطرق ضعيفة لا طائل تحتها، ولا إمكان للتعويل عليها منها أنهم قالوا: لو كان للعالم صانعان لكان كل واحد منهما قادرا لنفسه ويكون مقدور كل واحد منهما مقدور الآخر، فيقتضي هذا أن يصح أن يفعل أحدهما ويترك الآخر فيكون مفعولا متروكا موجودا معدوما وهذا محال وإثبات صانعين يؤدي إلى هذا، والمؤدي إلى المحال محال، وهذا الاستدلال فاسد لأن أحدهما لو أوجده صار موجودا، ولا يكون معدوما بترك الآخر، والامتناع عن الفعل لأنه كان معدوما ولم يتعلق عدمه به ألا ترى أن رجلين لو كانا قادرين على نقل خشبة من مكان إلى مكان فنقلها أحدهما وترك الآخر نقلها صارت منقولة بنقل الناقل، ولم يبق في المكان الأول بترك الآخر نقله، فكذا هذا.
And they clung to weak methods with no substance under them, and no possibility of relying upon them. Among them is that they said: If the world had two makers, each one of them would be powerful by himself, and the object of power of each one of them would be the object of power of the other. This would require that it could be that one of them acts and the other leaves [it], so it would be an acted-upon, left-aside, existing, non-existing thing, and this is impossible. And affirming two makers leads to this, and what leads to the impossible is impossible. And this inference is invalid because if one of them brought it into existence, it becomes existent, and it would not be non-existent by the leaving of the other. And abstention from the act is because it was non-existent, and its non-existence is not attached to him. Do you not see that if two men were able to move a piece of wood from a place to a place, and one of them moved it and the other left moving it, it becomes moved by the mover's moving, and it does not remain in the first place by the other's leaving moving it? So likewise this.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Mu'tazili argument against the possibility of multiple eternal creators. The Mu'tazila claim that if there were two makers, each would be omnipotent over the same objects, leading to a contradiction: if one creates something and the other does not, the thing would be both existing and non-existing. The author, Imam al-Nasafi, explains that this reasoning is invalid because if one creator brings something into existence, it simply exists; the other's inaction does not make it non-existent. The object's non-existence before creation is not attributable to the second creator's inaction. He provides an analogy: if two men can move a log, and one moves it while the other does nothing, the log is moved by the mover and does not remain in the original spot. Thus, no contradiction occurs. The refutation shows that the Mu'tazili argument fails to prove the impossibility of multiple creators.

Key Terms
صانعان
مقدور
محال
المعتزلة
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If there were two gods, one could create something while the other does not, resulting in the thing being both existing and non-existing simultaneously, which is impossible.
Correction: Imam al-Nasafi clarifies that if one creates, the thing simply exists; the other's inaction does not affect its existence. The non-existence prior to creation is not due to the second creator.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Imam al-Nasafi use to refute the Mu'tazili argument about two creators?
A) Two kings ruling one city
B) Two men moving a log
C) Two archers shooting an arrow
D) Two scribes writing one book

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili argument that two creators leads to contradiction is invalid because actual existence is determined by the one who acts, not by the one who refrains.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear an argument against your faith, do you immediately dismiss it or do you seek to understand its flaw as al-Nasafi did? Will you commit to studying the refutations of false arguments so that your faith is built on solid reasoning?
?
The Mu'tazila clung to weak methods. Are there any areas in your own understanding of Allah where you rely on weak reasoning or assumptions rather than sound knowledge? What will you do to correct that?
?
Al-Nasafi used an analogy to clarify his point. Do you take the time to explain Islamic beliefs to others in a clear, logical manner? How can you improve in conveying the truth with wisdom and sound argument?

Refuting Objections to Rational Proofs for Tawḥīd
Nasafi refutes an opponent's objection against rational proofs for tawḥīd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why dismissing rational proofs for God's unity is self-defeating and leads to blasphemous implications.

Core Idea
Rejecting rational proof for tawḥīd undermines all divine evidence.

Imam al-Nasafi here confronts a sophisticated objection against rational proofs for tawḥīd. The opponent claims that such proofs are rationally invalid. But Nasafi shows that this objection, if accepted, would force us to say that God taught His Prophet a faulty argument — an implication that is clearly blasphemous. This passage teaches us how kalam refutes objections by exposing their internal contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation to grasp the overall flow of the argument.
Notice the dense argumentative style; don't worry about every detail initially.
2
Identify the opponent's claim and first rebuttal
Find where Nasafi states the objection, then locate his first response: that this objection would imply God taught a flawed proof, leading to attributing ignorance or foolishness to God.
This is the key turning point of the argument.
3
Trace the consequences for scriptural proof
Follow how Nasafi extends the argument to show that accepting the objection also invalidates scriptural proof (samʿiyya) against shirk, because if God could be ignorant/foolish, then incapacity and lies become possible, destroying all evidence.
4
Understand the final conclusion about the opponent's intent
Nasafi concludes that the opponent's real aim is to destroy tawḥīd, prophethood, and religion entirely. Note how this reveals the stakes of the debate.
This shows the polemical context of the argument.

إرادة (۱) خلاف صاحبه وفي إرادة خلاف صاحبه خلاف معلومة، قيل له: إن أول ما نلزمك باعتراضك هذا تخطئة الله تعالى في تعليمه رسوله المبعوث صلى الله عليه وسلم لدعوة من اعتقد مع الله إلها آخر ودان بإثبات الشريك له دلائل الوحدانية واستحالة ألوهية من سواه من الأصنام والأوثان إذ ما علم من الدليل فاسد معترض لا دلالة فيه على ما استدل به عليه، إذ هو دليل عقلي ولا دلالة في العقل عليه، وليس في ثبوت العجز دلالة بطلان الألوهية فكان ما أثبته الله تعالى في القرآن وعلمه رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم من دلالة التوحيد وإبطال ألوهية من سواه ليحاج (٢) به من أعرض عنه وعانده فاسدا معترضا، ومن جوز على الله هذا فقد نسبه إلى الجهل والسفه لأنه تعالى إن لم يعلم بفساد هذا الدليل فهو جاهل، وإن علم بفساده، ومع ذلك علمه رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم ليحاج به من خالفه في التوحيد وتمسك بالشرك فهذا منه سفه و من وصف الله تعالى بالجهل والسفه فقد كفر من ساعته ثم أبطل على نفسه الدلالة السمعية على إبطال القول بالتثنية والشرك، وذلك لأنه لما جاز عليه الجهل والسفه ) (۳) وجاز أيضا عليه العجز عما هو مقدور في نفسه وزوال قدرته عما تعلقت به قدرة غيره على ما قررنا في تعذر إثبات الوحدانية على أصلهم بما ذكرنا من الدليلين قبل دلالة التمانع لجاز عليه الكذب وتأييد (٤) الكذب بالدلائل، ولما لم يخرج بذلك عن الألوهية واستحقاق العبادة، لا يخرج عن ذلك بهذا أيضا، ولعله أقام جميع المعجزات على أيدي الكاذبين وفيه إبطال الدليل السمعي أصلا، ولا دلالة في العقل على إثبات الوحدانية عنده، فإذا لا دليل عليه من حيث العقل ولا من حيث السمع، ولعل مراد هذا الملحد، إبطال الوحدانية وإفساد(۱) القول بالرسالة، ودفع الشرائع بأسرها وهدم قواعد الدين عن أصلها، ولولا هذا لكان إذا بَان له فساد مذهب القدرية، لإفضائها (۲) إلى إبطال القول بالوحدانية لتركها، وأخذ بمذاهب أهل الحق ولما صار إلى تقوية القول بالتثنية، وإبطال دلائل التوحيد وحيث لم ينقد للحق ولم يقر ببطلان ما كان عليه من المذاهب دل على أن مراده ما ذكرنا
Objection (1) contrary to its companion, and in intending contrary to its companion there is a known disagreement. It was said to him: The first thing we impose upon you by this objection is the error of God Almighty in the teaching of His Messenger - may God bless him and grant him peace - for the call of one who believed in another god with God and adhered to affirming the partner for Him, the proofs of oneness and the impossibility of divinity of others besides His from idols and statues, since what is known from the proof is corrupt, subject to objection, no indication in it for what it is used as evidence, because it is a rational proof and there is no indication in the intellect for it, and there is no indication in the existence of incapacity for the invalidity of divinity. So what God Almighty established in the Qur'an and taught His Messenger - peace be upon him - of the proof of tawḥīd and the nullification of the divinity of others besides Him to argue with those who turned away and opposed, would be corrupt and objectionable. And whoever permits this concerning God has attributed ignorance and foolishness to Him, because if He did not know the corruption of this proof, then He is ignorant, and if He knew its corruption and nonetheless taught it to His Messenger to argue with those who opposed in tawḥīd and adhered to shirk, then this is foolishness on His part, and whoever describes God Almighty with ignorance and foolishness has disbelieved immediately. Then he nullifies for himself the scriptural proof (al-dalāla al-samʿiyya) for the nullification of the claim of dualism and shirk. And that is because when ignorance and foolishness become permissible for Him, then also incapacity for what is possible in itself becomes permissible for Him, and the removal of His power over what the power of another is related to, as we established in the impossibility of establishing tawḥīd according to their principle by the two proofs we mentioned before the proof of mutual repulsion (al-tamānuʿ). Then lying becomes permissible for Him and the supporting of lies with proofs. And since He does not thereby exit from divinity and the deserving of worship, He does not exit from that by this also. Perhaps He performed all miracles at the hands of liars, and this entails the invalidation of scriptural proof entirely. And there is no indication in the intellect for establishing tawḥīd according to him. So there is no proof for it from the perspective of reason nor from the perspective of revelation. Perhaps this atheist's intent is to invalidate tawḥīd, corrupt the affirmation of prophethood, reject all laws, and demolish the foundations of religion from its roots. Were it not for this, when the corruption of the Qadariyya doctrine became clear to him, because it leads to the invalidation of the affirmation of tawḥīd by abandoning it, and he would have adopted the doctrines of the people of truth, and he would not have proceeded to strengthen the claim of dualism and invalidate the proofs of tawḥīd. And since he did not submit to truth and did not acknowledge the invalidity of what he was upon of doctrines, this indicates that his intent is what we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer format. The author begins by presenting an objection from an opponent who claims that the rational proof for tawḥīd is invalid. The author responds by showing that this objection would imply that God taught His Prophet a flawed proof, which would attribute ignorance and foolishness to God. Attributing such deficiencies to God is clear disbelief (kufr). The author then argues that acceptance of this objection would also invalidate the scriptural proof (al-dalāla al-samʿiyya) against dualism and shirk. Furthermore, if ignorance and foolishness are permissible for God, then incapacity and lying become permissible, leading to the absurdity that all miracles could be at the hands of liars. Thus, the opponent's position destroys both rational and scriptural evidence for tawḥīd. The author concludes that the opponent's true aim is to reject tawḥīd, prophethood, and religion entirely.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can reject rational proofs for God's existence without affecting the credibility of divine revelation.
Correction: Nasafi argues that rejecting rational proof leads to attributing ignorance/foolishness to God, which invalidates scriptural proof as well, showing that rational and revealed evidence are interconnected.

Checkpoint

A) It leads to attributing ignorance and foolishness to God.

D) It has no consequence.

Key Takeaway
The dismissal of rational proof for tawḥīd is not just a methodological error but leads to theological blasphemy and undermines all evidence for God.

Quranic Proof of Tawḥīd and Condemnation of the Opponent
Nasafi cites Quranic verses of tamānu' and condemns the opponent's inconsistency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses the Quranic tamānu' verses to argue for tawḥīd and why the opponent's position is self-contradictory and blasphemous.

Core Idea
The Quran proves tawḥīd through the tamānu' argument; to reject it is absurd and blasphemous.

Nasafi here confronts those who claim to uphold tawḥīd yet reject the very proofs that establish it. He expresses astonishment at their audacity and then directly cites the Quranic verses that refute polytheism through the tamānu' argument. This passage shows how scriptural proof reinforces rational necessity, and how dismissing it would imply absurdities about God.

Guided Path
1
Read the denunciation
Notice Nasafi's strong language against the opponent's self-contradiction: they call themselves Ahl al-ʿAdl wa al-Tawḥīd while holding a flawed creed.
2
Identify the Quranic verses
Locate the two verses quoted (21:22 and 23:91) and understand their meaning: if multiple gods existed, there would be corruption and each god would take what he created.
These verses constitute the scriptural proof (dalīl samʿī) for tawḥīd.
3
Understand the argument
Nasafi argues that if the opponent insists on rational proof only and rejects these verses, then teaching the Prophet to use such flawed arguments would make God foolish—a blasphemous impossibility.
This is a reductio ad absurdum exposing the opponent's inconsistency.
4
Reflect on the consequences
The passage ends with a severe warning: anyone attributing such flaws to God deserves severe punishment. Consider why such strong language is used to defend tawḥīd.

Source Text

ثم العجب أنه مع هذه العقيدة يلقب نفسه أهل العدل والتوحيد، وهذا هو آية الوقاحة وقلة الحياء والدين، وأعجب من هذا كله أنه لم يعدم من يتبعه على هذا الرأي البادي عواره والظاهر فساده الهادم لقواعد الدين المؤيد لأقاويل الملحدين، ويرضى به إماما يعتمد عليه ويلقي مقاليد أمور دينه إليه. والله تعالى يعصمنا عن قول يفضي إلى الإلحاد، ويصوننا من الزيغ عن سبيل الرشاد ثم يقال له: أليس أن الله قال : لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا الهَهُ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَنَا (٤) وقال عز وجل : وَمَا كَانَ مَعَهُ مِنْ إِلَهِ إِذَا لَذَهَبَ كُلُّ إِلَم بِمَا خَلَقَ (1) وما ذكر من الآيات التي مر ذكرها، ولا شك أن علو البعض على البعض وفساد السماوات والأرض غير متصور مع الاتفاق في الإرادة فلو كان الاختلاف فيها غير متصور لكان الله تعالى معلما رسوله لولا أن يحاج المشركين بما لا يصلح أن يكون دليلا، وكذا بتعليمه إياه محاجة الكفرة بالدليل العقلي، مع أنه لا دلالة فيه على ذلك كان سفيها جاهلا، ومن نسب الله تعالى إلى شيء من ذلك (۷) كان ممن لا يخفى كفره على أحد، ولوجب على أقرب الناس إليه إبانة رأسه عن جسده وقطع مادة شره عن ضعفاء المسلمين.
Then the wonder is that despite this creed he labels himself as belonging to Ahl al-ʿAdl wa al-Tawḥīd (the People of Justice and Oneness), and this is the utmost shamelessness, lack of modesty and religion. And more wonderful than all this is that he does not lack followers on this opinion, whose fault is evident and whose corruption is apparent, which demolishes the foundations of religion and supports the sayings of atheists. And he (the opponent) is accepted as an imam to rely upon and the reins of one's religious affairs are handed over to him. May God protect us from a saying that leads to atheism, and keep us from deviation from the path of guidance. Then it is said to him: Did not God say: 'If there were in them gods besides Allah, they would have been corrupted' (21:22) and He, Mighty and Majestic, said: 'Nor was there with Him any god; then each god would have taken what he created' (23:91) and other verses that have been mentioned. And there is no doubt that the superiority of some over others and the corruption of the heavens and the earth are inconceivable with agreement in will. So if disagreement in the will were inconceivable, then God would be teaching His Messenger, unless He were to argue with the polytheists by what is not suitable as evidence. Likewise, by teaching him to argue with the disbelievers by the rational proof, while there is no indication in it for that, He would be foolish and ignorant. And whoever attributes anything like that to God Almighty, his disbelief is not hidden from anyone, and it would be incumbent upon his closest people to separate his head from his body and cut off the source of his evil from the weak Muslims.

Commentary
This passage begins with the author expressing amazement at the opponent's audacity: despite holding a creed that undermines tawḥīd, he calls himself 'Ahl al-ʿAdl wa al-Tawḥīd' (the Mu'tazilite self-designation). The author condemns him and those who follow him. Then the author addresses the opponent directly, asking: did God not reveal verses that prove tawḥīd? He quotes Sūrat al-Anbiyā' 21:22 and Sūrat al-Mu'minūn 23:91, which show that if multiple gods existed, there would be corruption and conflict. The author argues that if the opponent insists that only rational proofs are valid and these scriptural proofs are insufficient, then teaching the Prophet to use such flawed rational arguments would make God foolish—an impossibility that exposes the opponent's position as absurd and blasphemous. The passage ends with a strong denunciation: anyone who attributes such flaws to God deserves severe punishment.

Refuting the Objection to the Proof of One God
Refutation of an objection against the proof of one God

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the proof that two gods are impossible does not invalidate the lordship of the one God, and the key distinction between necessary and impossible existence.

Core Idea
The proof for one God establishes impossibility of a second, not invalidation of the first.

In this passage, the author answers an objection: if the proof for one God shows that two gods are impossible, why doesn't it also apply to the one God? He explains the crucial difference between invalidating what is necessarily existent and proving the non-existence of what is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then the English translation. Let the flow of the argument sink in.
Notice the logical progression from objection to resolution.
2
Identify the objection
The opponent claims that the proof for one God would also remove both or one from lordship. Understand why this seems plausible.
The objection is based on a misunderstanding of the proof's scope.
3
Follow the author's logical steps
The author first establishes the Maker through originated things, then considers a second maker, and concludes its impossibility using the argument from mutual impotence.
The key move is that the proof shows impossibility of two, not invalidity of the one.
4
Grasp the key distinction
The author distinguishes between invalidating something that is impossible to invalidate (the one God's lordship, which is necessary) and proving the impossibility of something for which no existence is proven (a second god).
This distinction resolves the objection.
5
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Many mistakenly think the same reasoning that disproves two gods would apply to one God. The author shows this is a false analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول له: أما حل الشبهة أن ما ذكرتم من الدلالة يخرجهما أو أحدهما عن الربوبية، وذلك محال كما قلتم فى الواحد أنه لا يوصف بالقدرة على الكذب، فهو أن هذا تمويه فإن المستحيل هو إبطال ربوبية من ثبتت ربوبيته ولم تثبت ربوبية اثنين ليكون ما يوجب بطلان ذلك مستحيلا بل علم ثبوت الصانع للعالم بدلالة المحدثات، ثم أخطرنا بالبال أن صانعا آخر جائز الوجود أو ممتنع الوجود، فتأملنا فعلمنا أنه ممتنع الوجود لما مر أنه لو كان مع الله إله آخر لكانا جميعا عاجزين أو كان أحدهما عاجزا، والعاجز لا يصلح أن يكون إلها، فكان ذلك دليل أن لا يتصور ثبوت صانعين، فلم يكن هذا دليلا يوجب بطلان ربوبية من ثبتت ربوبيته بل ذلك دليل استحالة ثبوت صانعين بخلاف صانع واحد، لأنه تثبت ربوبيته بالدليل الموجب، وبطلان ربوبية من تثبت ربوبيته محال لكون ربوبيته واجب الوجود مستحيل العدم فمن لم يعرف الفرق بين إبطال ما هو مستحيل البطلان وبين امتناع ثبوت ما وجد دليل امتناعه فهو قليل الحظ من العلم بالحقائق
Then we say to him: As for the resolution of the sophism: that what you mentioned of the proof would remove both or one of them from lordship, and that is impossible as you said concerning the One that He cannot be described with power over lying: this is deception. For the impossible is only the invalidation of the lordship of one whose lordship is established, while the lordship of two has not been established so that what necessitates its invalidation would be impossible. Rather, we know the existence of the Maker of the world through the proof of originated things. Then we considered in mind that another maker is either possible of existence or impossible of existence. We reflected and knew that He is impossible of existence because of what has passed: that if there were with God another god, both would be powerless or one would be powerless, and the powerless is not fit to be a god. So that was a proof that the existence of two makers is inconceivable. So this was not a proof that necessitates the invalidation of the lordship of one whose lordship is established, but rather that proof is the impossibility of the existence of two makers, unlike the case of one Maker, because His lordship is established by a positive proof, and the invalidation of the lordship of one whose lordship is established is impossible because His lordship is necessary of existence, impossible of non-existence. So whoever does not know the difference between invalidating what is impossible to invalidate and between the impossibility of the existence of something for which a proof of its impossibility has been found, he has little share of knowledge of realities.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage refutes an objection raised against the proof for the oneness of God. The opponent argued that the same reasoning used to prove one God would also apply to both gods, invalidating the lordship of either. The author explains that this is a misconception. The proof establishes the impossibility of two gods, not the invalidation of the already established lordship of the one true God. The author walks through the logic: we first know the Maker through the proof of originated things. Then we consider the possibility of a second maker, and through reason we find that it is impossible because if there were two gods, they would both be powerless or one would be powerless, which contradicts divinity. Thus, the proof shows the impossibility of two makers, not that the established Maker's lordship is invalid. The key distinction is between invalidating something already proven impossible to invalidate (like the lordship of the one true God) and proving the non-existence of something for which a proof of impossibility exists (like a second god). The author chides those who cannot grasp this distinction.

امتناع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The same proof that disproves two gods would also disprove the one God.
Correction: The proof shows the impossibility of a second god, not the invalidity of the one God whose existence is necessary and established by positive proof.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the proof that two gods are impossible not invalidate the lordship of the one God?
A) Because the one God's lordship is already proven by a positive proof and is necessary of existence.
B) Because the proof only applies to the second god, not the first.
C) Because the one God is not subject to the same limitations.
D) Because the conclusion is hypothetical only.

Key Takeaway
The proof for one God shows the impossibility of a second god, not the invalidity of the one God whose existence is necessary and established by positive proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever doubted the existence of God because you felt you couldn't logically disprove every possible alternative god? How does this lesson's distinction between positive proof and impossibility challenge that doubt, and what would it cost you to now rely on the clear proof from creation?
?
The author says that whoever cannot differentiate between 'invalidating what is impossible to invalidate' and 'proving impossibility' has little share of knowledge of realities. Where in your own faith—perhaps in your certainty about Allah's attributes or your trust in His promises—do you confuse these two, and what step will you take today to be more precise?
?
If the lordship of Allah is established necessarily and cannot be invalidated, why do you still sometimes live as if His existence is uncertain—neglecting prayer, disobeying, or fearing people more than Him? What would change if you truly internalized that His lordship is absolute and impossible to negate?

The Proof of Tawhid from Power Necessitating Will
Nasafi argues that Qur'anic proofs against multiple gods rely on power which necessarily implies will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Qur'anic verses prove the impossibility of multiple gods by emphasizing the effectiveness of divine power, which necessarily implies will, and why contradiction in power logically entails contradiction in will.

Core Idea
Divine power necessitates will; contradiction in power proves tawhid.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla presents a sophisticated argument for tawhid (the oneness of God) rooted in the Qur'an. The author shows that key verses against multiple gods are not directly about will but about power (qudra), and that power cannot exist without will. Understanding this deductive chain is essential for appreciating the depth of classical Kalam reasoning on divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage from Nasafi carefully, then the literal translation. Let the author's own argument unfold.
Notice the dense, logical style typical of Kalam texts.
2
Identify the Qur'anic verses cited
Find each verse referenced and note how Nasafi uses them to argue from power, not from will directly.
Verses include 21:22, 23:91, 6:46, 10:107, and 39:38.
3
Understand the distinction between power and will
Nasafi clarifies that some verses that mention 'will' actually refer to the act (fi'l), not the attribute of will. This is crucial to avoid misinterpreting the proof.
The key is that the context speaks of removing harm, which is an act, not will itself.
4
Follow the logical chain from power to will
The author argues that power cannot be executed without will, so will is necessarily established. Then, if two gods existed, their powers would conflict, leading to a contradiction in will as well.
This relies on the concept of mutalazimayn (necessary concomitants).
5
Reflect on the conclusion: impossibility of multiple gods
The entire argument demonstrates that the very concept of multiple gods entails contradiction in both power and will, which is incompatible with divinity.
Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini's statement reinforces that the proof ascends from power to will.

إن من المعلوم الذي لا ريب فيه أن الاستدلال بقوله تعالى: ﴿ لَوْ كَانَ فِيهِمَا آلِهَةٌ إِلَّا اللَّهُ لَفَسَدَتَا ﴾ وبقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَمَا اتَّخَذَ اللَّهُ مِنْ وَلَدٍ وَمَا كَانَ مَعَهُ مِنْ إِلَهٍ إِذًا لَذَهَبَ كُلُّ إِلَهٍ بِمَا خَلَقَ وَلَعَلَا بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ ﴾ هو الاستدلال بنفاذ قدرة كل منهم، لما أن كلا منهم يفعل غير ما يفعل من وراءه من الآلهة، وتنفذ قدرته فيما يوجب علو أمره وظهور ملكه وسلطانه، وكذا بقوله تعالى: ﴿ قُلْ أَرَأَيْتُمْ إِنْ أَخَذَ اللَّهُ سَمْعَكُمْ وَأَبْصَارَكُمْ وَخَتَمَ عَلَى قُلُوبِكُمْ مَنْ إِلَهٌ غَيْرُ اللَّهِ يَأْتِيكُمْ بِهِ ﴾ الآية، وكذا بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَإِنْ يَمْسَسْكَ اللَّهُ بِضُرٍ فَلَا كَاشِفَ لَهُ إِلَّا هُوَ ﴾، فأما الاستدلال بقوله: ﴿ وَإِنْ يُرِدْكَ بِخَيْرٍ ﴾ وكذا بقوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنْ أَرَادَنِيَ اللَّهُ بِضُرٍ ﴾ وقوله ﴿ أَوْ أَرَادَنِي بِرَحْمَةٍ ﴾ فالمراد من ذلك هو الفعل لا الإرادة ألا ترى أنه قال: ﴿ هَلْ هُنَّ كَاشِفَاتُ ضُرِّهِ ﴾، ﴿ هَلْ هُنَّ مُمْسِكَاتُ رَحْمَتِهِ ﴾ وإنما يحتاج إلى الكشف والإمساك بعد الفعل لا بعد الإرادة فإذا كان التعليق بالقدرة وإثبات العجز غير، إذ تنفيذ القدرة لن يكون بدون الإرادة، فكانت هي ثابتة ضرورة بثبوت القدرة على ما هو الحكم في المتلازمين، وقد أقمنا الدلالة على أن خروج المقدور عن القدرة يكون عن عجز، وذلك منافي للربوبية، فكانت من ضرورة وقوع التعارض في القدرة لو كان اثنين وقوع التعارض في الإرادة إذ هي لا تمتاز عن القدرة وكل ما يمتاز عن القدرة فليس بإرادة بل هو تمني والقديم غير موصوف به لأنه من أمارات العجز، ولهذا قال أبو إسحاق الأسفراييني بعدما حكي اعتراض أبي هاشم على الإرادة: وليس هذا وجه الاستدلال به لكنه ما قدمنا من تحقيق القدرة ونفي النقيصة ثم يرتقي منه إلى الإرادة أي لما ثبت التعارض في القدرة وتعطلت قدرتهما أو قدرة أحدهما ثبت ذلك في الإرادة
Indeed, it is known without doubt that the inference by His statement, the Most High: 'If there were in them other gods besides Allah, they would have been corrupted' and by His statement, the Most High: 'And Allah has not taken any son, nor was there any god with Him; then each god would have taken what he created and some of them would have risen over others' is the inference by the effectiveness of the power (nufadh al-qudra) of each of them, because each of them does other than what the gods behind him do, and his power is effective in what necessitates the highness of his command and the appearance of his dominion and authority. And likewise by His statement, the Most High: 'Say: Have you considered if Allah were to take away your hearing and your sight and seal your hearts, which god other than Allah could bring them to you?' the verse, and likewise by His statement, the Most High: 'And if Allah touches you with harm, there is no remover of it except Him.' As for the inference by His statement: 'And if He intends you good' and likewise by His statement, the Most High: 'If Allah intends me harm' and His statement: 'or intends me mercy,' the intended meaning of that is the act (al-fi'l), not the will (al-irada). Do you not see that He said: 'Are they removers of His harm?' and 'Are they restrainers of His mercy?' And the need for removal and restraint is only after the act, not after the will. So if the attachment is to power and the establishment of inability (al-'ajz) is other, since the execution of power cannot be without will, then it (will) is necessarily established by the establishment of power, according to the rule for the two necessary concomitants (al-mutalazimayn). And we have established the evidence that the leaving of the predetermined thing (al-maqdur) out of power results from inability, and that is contrary to lordship (al-rububiyya). So it is a necessary consequence of the occurrence of contradiction (al-ta'arud) in power—if there were two—the occurrence of contradiction in will, since it (will) is not distinct from power, and whatever is distinct from power is not will but rather wish (tamanni), and the Eternal is not described with it because it is one of the signs of inability. And for this reason Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini said, after relating the objection of Abu Hashim concerning will: 'This is not the aspect of inference with it, but rather what we have presented of the verification of power and the negation of deficiency, then one ascends from it to will,' meaning that when contradiction in power is established and their power or the power of one of them becomes inoperative, then that is established in will.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument establishing that the Qur'anic proofs against the existence of multiple gods are based on the concept of power (qudra) and necessarily imply will (irada). The author, Imam Nasafi, begins by stating that it is indisputable that verses such as (21:22) and (23:91) are used to infer the impossibility of multiple gods through the effectiveness of each god's power. If there were multiple gods, each would act independently and seek to dominate, leading to corruption and conflict. He then mentions similar verses (6:46, 10:107) that also point to power. However, he clarifies that verses mentioning 'will' (irada) like (10:107) and (39:38) actually refer to action (fi'l), not will, because the context speaks of removing or restraining harm, which are actions subsequent to will. The true argument is that the verses about power prove the impossibility of two gods, and since power cannot be executed without will, the contradiction in power necessitates a contradiction in will. Nasafi reinforces this by stating that a being's inability to execute power is a sign of deficiency ('ajz), incompatible with lordship (rububiyya). Therefore, if two gods existed, their powers would conflict, and that conflict must extend to their wills because will is not separate from power—if it were separate, it would be mere wish (tamanni), which is a sign of inability and not attributable to the Eternal. He concludes by citing Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, who confirms that the proof begins with power and ascends to will: once contradiction in power is established, it necessarily entails contradiction in will.

Key Terms
قدرة (qudra)
إرادة (irada)
تعارض (ta'arud)
عجز ('ajz)
ربوبية (rububiyya)
فعل (fi'l)
تمني (tamanni)
متلازمين (mutalazimayn)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Qur'anic verses about God's will directly prove tawhid.
Correction: The verses actually prove through power, and will follows necessarily from power. The proof is not directly from will but from the implications of power.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do the Qur'anic verses like 'If there were in them other gods besides Allah, they would have been corrupted' primarily argue against multiple gods?
A) Because they show that multiple gods would have conflicting wills.
B) Because they demonstrate that each god's power would be ineffective.
C) Because they indicate that each god's power would be fully effective, leading to conflict and corruption.
D) Because they prove that only one god can have will.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'anic proof against multiple gods relies on the effectiveness of power, which necessarily entails will; any contradiction in power implies contradiction in will, making multiple gods impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's power and will are necessarily inseparable, does your prayer life reflect a trust that God's will is always backed by His ability—or do you sometimes doubt that He can do what He has promised?
?
The passage warns that a will distinct from power is mere wish (tamanni), a mark of inability. In what area of your life are you treating God's will as a passive wish rather than an active decree, and how can you align your heart with His perfect power?
?
The argument shows that multiple 'gods' create internal contradiction. Have you allowed any desire, fear, or ambition to function as a competing 'god' in your heart, producing conflict in your decisions? How does this truth drive you to single-hearted devotion to Allah alone?

The Inseparability of Power and Will and the Impossibility of Two Gods
The author proves the inseparability of divine power and will to refute the possibility of two gods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why divine power (qudra) and will (irāda) are inseparable and how this proves that two gods cannot coexist.

Core Idea
Power and will are inseparable; conflict in one means conflict in both, so two gods are impossible.

This passage from Imam al-Nasafi builds a key proof for tawḥīd by showing that divine power and will are necessarily linked. The author argues that if two gods existed, their powers would conflict, leading to inability — and since will is not distinct from power, conflict in will follows necessarily. This lesson unpacks the argument, clarifying how Quranic verses are interpreted and why mere wish (tamannī) cannot be attributed to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Note the Quranic verses cited and the author's reasoning flow.
The passage is dense; take your time to follow the argument.
2
Identify the core claim
Find where the author states that power and will are inseparable (mutalāzimān). Understand that if power is established, will is necessarily established too.
Look for the phrase 'as is the rule for inseparable correlates.'
3
Follow the proof for two gods
The author argues that if two gods existed, their powers would conflict, leading to inability (ʿajz). Since will is not distinct from power, conflict in will also occurs, making both gods incapable — impossible for lordship.
4
Understand the distinction from wish
The author distinguishes true will from mere wish (tamannī), which is a sign of inability and not attributable to Allah. This reinforces that divine will is perfect and inseparable from power.
Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini is cited to support this argument.
5
Reflect on the theological conclusion
The impossibility of two gods is proven because their powers and wills would conflict, leading to deficiency. This argument strengthens the Islamic belief in absolute divine unity (tawḥīd).
The passage ends with 'And Allah is the Grantor of success.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الآية، وكذا بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَإِن يَمْسَسْكَ اللهُ بِضُرٍ فَلَا كَاشِفَ لَهُ إِلَّا هُوَ ()، فأما الاستدلال بقوله: ﴿وَإِن يُردّكَ يغير ( (٣) وكذا بقوله تعالى إِنْ أَرَادَنِيَ اللَّهُ بِضُي ) (۳) وقوله أَوْ أَرَادَنِي بِرَحْمَةٍ (٤) فالمراد من ذلك هو الفعل لا الإرادة ألا ترى أنه قال: . ،(٥) هَلْ هُنَّ كَشِفَتُ ضُرِّهِ } () ، هَلْ هُنَ مُمْسِكَتُ رَحْمَتِهِ () وإنما يحتاج إلى الكشف والإمساك بعد الفعل لا بعد الإرادة فإذا كان التعليق بالقدرة وإثبات العجز غيْر، إذ تنفيذ القدرة لن يكون بدون الإرادة، فكانت هي ثابتة ضرورة بثبوت القدرة على ما هو الحكم في المتلازمين، وقد أقمنا الدلالة على أن خروج المقدور عن القدرة يكون عن عجز، وذلك منافي للربوبية، فكانت (۷) من ضرورة وقوع التعارض في القدرة (لو) كان اثنين وقوع التعارض في الإرادة إذ هي لا تمتاز عن القدرة ) (۸) وكل ما يمتاز عن القدرة فليس (۹) بإرادة بل هو تَمَنِّ والقديم غير موصوف به لأنه من أمارات العجز ، ولهذا قال أبو إسحاق (۱۰) الأسفراييني بعدما حكي اعتراض أبي هاشم على الإرادة: وليس هذا وجه الاستدلال به لكنه ما قدمنا من تحقيق القدرة (۱۱) ونفي النقيصة ثم يرتقي (۱۲) منه إلى الإرادة أي لما ثبت التعارض في القدرة وتعطلت قدرتهما أو قدرة أحدهما ، ثبت ذلك في الإرادة ضرورة استحالة امتيازهما إذ ما امتازت عنه الإرادة اضطرارا وليس بقدرة (١) ، والله الموفق.
The verse, and likewise by His statement: {And if Allah touches you with harm, there is no remover of it except Him} (Qur'an 10:107). As for the argument by His statement: {And if He intends you some harm} (Qur'an 39:38) and likewise by His statement: {If Allah intends me with harm} (Qur'an 39:38) and His statement: {or intends me with mercy} (Qur'an 39:38), the intended meaning of that is the action, not the will. Do you not see that He said: {Are they the removers of His harm?} (Qur'an 39:38), {Are they the withholders of His mercy?} (Qur'an 39:38). And need for removal and withholding is only after the action, not after the will. So when the conditional clause is linked to power and the affirmation of inability is not possible, because the execution of power cannot be without will, so it (will) is necessarily established by the establishment of power, as is the rule for inseparable correlates. And we have adduced the proof that the exiting of the object of power from power occurs due to inability, and that is incompatible with lordship. So it (i.e., will) is necessarily from the necessity of the occurrence of conflict in power were there two (gods). The occurrence of conflict in will (is also necessary) because it (will) is not distinct from power. And everything that is distinct from power is not will but rather wish, and the Eternal is not described by it because it is one of the signs of inability. For this reason Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini said, after narrating the objection of Abu Hashim regarding will: 'This is not the way of argument by it, but rather what we have presented of the verification of power and the denial of deficiency, then one ascends from it to will.' That is, when conflict in power is established and their power becomes incapacitated, or the power of one of them, that is established in will necessarily, because it is impossible for them to be distinct, since whatever the will is distinct from is necessarily not power. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a proof of tawhid (divine unity) by demonstrating the necessary connection between divine power (qudra) and will (irāda). It begins by citing Quranic verses that speak of Allah's power to remove harm or grant mercy. The author argues that these verses refer to actions, not will, because the ability to remove or withhold only makes sense after an action exists. However, the conditional link (taʿlīq) in these verses is actually tied to power (qudra), and since the execution of power requires will, the existence of will is necessarily implied by the existence of power—they are inseparable correlates (mutalāzimān). If there were two gods, their powers would conflict, leading to the inability of one or both to act, which is impossibility (ʿajz) and incompatible with divinity (rubūbiyya). Because will is not distinct from power (lā tamtāzu ʿan al-qudra), conflict in power necessitates conflict in will. Any supposed will that is distinct from power is actually mere wish (tamannī), which is a sign of inability and not attributable to the Eternal. The author then cites Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, who states that the correct argument begins by establishing the reality of power and denying any deficiency, then ascends to will. The conclusion: if conflict in power is proven, conflict in will follows necessarily, because the two attributes cannot be separated. The passage ends with 'And Allah is the Grantor of success.'

Key Terms
إرادة (irāda)
قدرة (qudra)
تعارض (taʿāruḍ)
عجز (ʿajz)
ربوبية (rubūbiyya)
متلازمين (mutalāzimayn)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Divine will can be considered independently of divine power.
Correction: Will and power are inseparable; conflict in power necessarily entails conflict in will, so if two gods had conflicting powers, their wills would also conflict, which is impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, why must conflict in will necessarily follow from conflict in power?
A) Because will is independent of power.
B) Because will is not distinct from power.
C) Because will is a sign of ability.
D) Because power is derived from will.

Key Takeaway
The inseparability of divine power and will shows that two gods cannot exist, as their powers would conflict and lead to inability, which contradicts divinity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation beyond your control, do you truly believe that no one but Allah can remove harm or grant mercy? Or do you secretly rely on other means as if they had independent power? Reflect on a recent difficulty—did your heart turn to Allah alone, or did you look to others as if they could change your fate? Commit to making your du'a exclusive to Allah today.
?
The lesson shows that any separation between will and power reduces will to mere wish. Examine your own intentions: are your desires backed by the conviction that Allah alone has power to fulfill them, or are they empty wishes unaccompanied by trust in His qudra? What wish can you transform into a sincere supplication today?
?
Two gods are impossible because conflict leads to inability. In your own life, when you try to serve multiple masters—pleasing people, seeking status, chasing desires—does that inner conflict render you spiritually powerless? How can you realign your will to single-hearted devotion to Allah, the only One whose power is without deficiency?
